des poilz des papieres	Sei tornato su un tema più leggero!
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When the eyelashes are born in a way that is not natural and are inflamed, if they harm the eyes, and bring on mannerisms of diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albugine, to such an extent that it causes destruction to the eyes; and the treatment follows four manners: or by applying fire cautery, or by using a cooling medicine according to what is written in the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and suturing or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the chief part of the patient's face in your hand, then turn the eyelash paper around your left hand; if it has turned, it is good; if not, take one needle with all .i. thread above and place it near the edge of the eyelash paper or where the hairs grow near these hairs, and draw .i. thread up to all the eyelash paper, and turn it at a razor; then make in the part below the eyelash paper, below the inflamed hairs, with all the spatula cutting, from the large tear well to the small one; then pull out one thread, and put under the eyelash paper a small tent of cotton and fabric, then sign above the eyelash paper a shape like the myrtle leaf, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the eyelashes raise which are divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If there is need to tie with paper, take a great quantity of the paper according as it is softened; then apply to all the spasm above the two lines that you have signed, and begin from a large tear down to small; and one of the incisions should be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the thread into one of the two angles where it is curved, then scrape off all of it; then join together the two lips with a seam made by an awl on a whole thin thread of wool, and suck out the blood, and make dry the superfluity of threads above the two sorcerers on any gluey things, if you see this to be done; and if not, do not bother, then leave the seam and threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without a seam with things drying and constraining, for the paper revives with the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is loose (as the ancients said), and this work is done without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you sign on the paper a figure which will be like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at three cut threads according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then draw what rises above the small forces equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal in length, then take a needle with thread on it, and insert the end of the thread into the skin; and insert the other thread close to the large wound, and the second thread close to the small one, and assemble between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over which you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then calm it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are changed: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches in both cases are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the eyelids is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two canthuses by art, and two thin ligaments as long as the paper and as wide as the thickness of the eyelid; and draw on the two cheeks from both parts where you hold the threads; then gather one and the other subtly above what rises from the paper of oil, and strain the two canthuses from the two parts formed; and leave it for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and blacken and dry out, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, if the ulcer has some strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper gauze has been lifted, and the hairs cannot stick anymore; and that is the shape of the two canines you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The stitches are as follows: you take a very fine needle, and insert one thread of soft silk into it; then gather the cheeks and tie each one subtly, and make the length of the threads about the width of an outstretched hand; then order in the chase another thread of thin silk quickly, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in a healthy state; and place them in the sun so that the stitches are illuminated, because this is a very fine and subtle stitch; then insert the needle all around the root of the hair next to it, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you pull it out over the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it reaches the thread in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrow is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the arrow downwards to the entire length that you have ordained, until the arrow comes out through the pores above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will pull out the arrow and thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, so that the hair grows in its place and the flesh heals; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long hair of the natural beard, and raise with that which you leave, until it is elongated and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the purtenance comes to the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through a sudden blow of a wound, or a cut, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working with it is that you split apart the sudden wound, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie so that it is healed; and it is not necessary for you to use in its cure things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than the first; but there is a working with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the flower of water or hollyhock and flaxseed are cooked, and unguents made from honey melted in some oil, and I envelop it in a tent, and cure it with those.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you watch out so that it does not heal back to its original form; and these treatments we have mentioned are only preventive measures against this disease from coming back in its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes into the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below, is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and a cut and a cautery and similar things; and the way of doing it is that you take a needle, in which there are double threads, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left to right as far as right, so that the thread comes out on both sides of the flesh; then let the flesh above go over all the needle, and the handle at the wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back according to what is needed, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on both sides inside the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and so make an angle such that when they are assembled, the shape is as the shape of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its edges are swollen beneath, from what is in front of the paper; then join together the two severed parts, and sew with a thread of linen; then apply the cure of those things that we have said about soothing medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from tear or cut or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one should do the work according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare remedies from all their power to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs to be treated with and the instruments, in several dispositions.

de l’ungle de l’oil	The infection of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is noted that the infection of the eye can be in two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nervous but resembles a white frozen congealed moisture, which when touched with iron and thought to be cut with forceps cannot be done; and both appearances begin near the main tear duct and grow bit by bit until it covers all of the eye, its light, and its movement.
