de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems like you're reading from a medieval medical text again!
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The red eye of some men appears at times, and covers the pupil and holds on the papers and turns to the outside, and seems like a rose made of marble; and the work is such that the patient puts his head in vinegar, then he works the eyes, and coils all that flesh with the needles suitable for it, and sustains it with force; then cuts the first flesh, and goes on cutting to the razor until the end, and be careful not to damage the eye during the operation; and let the incision have the shape we have said in the incision of the stone and with the small forces that one removes the scab, as the form shows after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of red nettle or similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and put cotton on the outside of the eye with egg white, so that it is sure of hot aposteme; and if there remains nothing, and the blood pressure subsides, and you doubt hot aposteme, then leave the eye and cure the hot aposteme with soothing things; then return to your operation until it is healed, and thus treat all flesh that is stuck in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Mais il faut toujours prendre soin de soulager les cures de chaque œil faible suivant la voie naturelle, et celle qui est accidentelle, en opérations de fer ; et ne pas mettre ta main dans aucun de ces opérations tant que tu ne vois pas que le membre soit suffisamment soulagé de celui-là opération.
des voines des eulz	from the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red spots that are covered on the eye, and they hinder the work of sight and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for the doctor that he looks at whether the eye itself has a bevel on it, if so, and there is no other foreign disease except the bevel; then cut into it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head over your vein, then suspend those veins up to the entire length according to his wisdom, and the veins should be very fine and double according to this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two needles be by degrees in one place according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then treat the eye by pulling those veins gently, and suck out the blood every hour afterwards, until you see those veins being removed from the eye; and be careful not to touch the eye with the points of your spatulae, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss any of those veins; and when you have done that, make some green and red juice drop into the eye to corrupt what remains in the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to treat all of this in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains have subsided and you are assured that the abscess is hot, then start again in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems we've reached the end of a medieval medical text discussing eye treatments. The title "de la fistule de l'oil" translates to "of the fistula of the eye". A fistula is an abnormal connection or passageway between two normally separate body parts, and in this case, it's likely referring to a chronic infection or abscess affecting the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor's instruments are called "arissati" fistules: when you cure it with fire and a hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you must make an incision on the abscess where it should die, and extract all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument by which this shape is made; and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron to a pointy tip, and be sharpened like a file as much as in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is reduced; and do this as many times, then restore the place with medicated poultices.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the abscess is closed and pus forms and the body of the boil is closed and remains so for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not an abscess, and a bad accident does not occur, know that he is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to bring the fistula back to its original place according to this shape: and you will uncover from bone the second time with iron, and by sharp remedies, and when it has been uncovered, take out the iron rod according to this shape, and let the iron rod have 3 angles, and the shaft be thinned up to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone next to the wound, and move your hand away from the eye I poke, then turn completely back to the forest until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels by what the vein goes in if he holds his hand on his head; and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens at the site, then remove the material from the head; and this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the pus of the wound
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the pus has completely drained from the wound and there is no further disturbance or decrease in size, it is necessary to tie up the patient; then clean the wound, then apply leeches with iron needles to suck, then put a poultice made of aloe, incense, and sarcocolle on top of the wound; then strain the wound by wrapping it with bandages and cloths; and the way to do this is to take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to how much pus the wound needs to be drained; then strain from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the leeches to suck without causing further injury; then remove the leeches and leave the wound strained day and night; and if you see the poultice become wet, it is necessary to tighten it more; then remove the poultice after the next day and night; and if you see the wound recovering, it is good; if not, then repeat the poulticing and bandaging and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the rupture of a membrane or skin ( possibly referring to a specific medical condition)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the membrane (toile uvee) ruptures and bursts open, and comes out in pieces like a grain of resin, and it's terrifying to see; then if you see it covering, the treatment is such that you insert an needle into the root of the lower part up to the top, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the wound; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle in place; then cut the thread and tie one part of the membrane around, and tighten it well, then extract the needle and put a piece of linen moistened with egg on top of the wound; and let it be until the thread sticks to the membrane, then dress the wound with comforting things until the pain is healed; and at any time the wound is restrained by the membrane each part in a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus appears in a great abundance, then make it pierce with a fine needle that comes from the center of the eye, and drain the moistened albuginum (a part of the eye) and descend into the pus, and enter inside as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the cornea of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an eye which is assembled in the eye, appearing like a vein descending, and it's not a vein; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and pull it until you see the bow or thread come up to your eyes; then it should be fixed, and not descend, and let go the lightness, and look at the things as the patient usually sees them; and if it does not descend below, know that it is a vein, and if the descent of the thread from the bow is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If thou makest the patient sit between thy hands, then take the subtle spatulum and place it above the corneal tissue I over the conjunctiva with the cornea, so that the bowels issue; and when they are issued, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then be treated with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the tears of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have known the similarities of waters in division and what needs to be pierced; do it according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from light for the sun, and close the sound eye very tightly; then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a nail on that white part of the eye at the smallest tear corner; then thrust the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and twist your hand until it pierces through the white part of the eye, and feel when almagda comes out empty; and it is necessary that the measure of the way to almagda be exactly at the depth of the measure of an espace which is from the prunelet to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the conjunctiva, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, then express it under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, then he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the water ascends again through the second vessel, put the force with the instrument, and when it is well positioned and does not ascend, then pull gently on the thread loop turning your hand slowly back and forth; and then place a drop of gem oil in the water and lift the eye from inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put a cloth soaked in rose oil and linen moistened with egg white over the eye, and tie it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, put a lint pad with abundance of egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are very hard, then you must take the instrument that is called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva alone, and don't go too deep, but make it subtle, then insert as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient to sleep in a suitable bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head or to the right or left, and keep him tied according to his condition just until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and examine his vision, and make him see some things, and then remove the bandage until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but rather delay it because the water ascends quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	An abscess forms, instruct the patient to discharge their eye on the seventh day, and use a poultice that soothes an abscess; and when it is calmed, untie the bandage and place a green leaf on its face to cover for any day, and be in this dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go away from the house to and fro, and become familiar with their cases; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iarach (a place in medieval times), who said that in his peaceful land they used to make alum incisions, through which the liquid would come out, but somehow I never saw anyone do it in our territory, nor did I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alum (algarde), because those who do not know them see them; and they are made of pure silver (or more likely, white lead or some other metal)
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads be of the same subtle appearance, and their ends in three sharp points (or corners).
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the skin
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are or appear various kinds of boils that look like scorpions in many places; and if it has such ones where the boil is inflamed with foul colour, and if it has a boil of good colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then for the boil that is good and not inflamed, it is necessary that you have the patient sit between your hands in the direction of the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice on those boils, and treat them with fire; then take what you can grasp with a fine and sharp spatula from one side, until you know that that boil is completely opened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that you can't remove, then open it up completely with the sharp instruments (likely meaning scalpels or forceps), so that nothing is left; and if it's not swollen, or an abscess forms, then cut out the scab as needed; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize them until the swelling subsides and all the flesh bumps are removed; then pour oil on the navel area and drink water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle operates and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is clean; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a piece of linen thread thick enough, and knotted with three turns, with an interval of about two fingers between each knot; and put the patient's head on the thread so that it holds some power, and draw it into fragrance until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and children often do this in school, and it is a light thing to do for one who wants to do it; then take the head which comes out by the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know them one after the other while they are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know to be true that the newt has corrupted that flesh, then lead out the young one, let out the blood, and wet the cord in Egyptian oil, and put it back again at night just as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointments have corroded all that remains of flesh; and then put on a poultice of some kind for a few days until they are healed, and if they need dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, by which one distills oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or white metal, resembling an open lamp or candle holder, with a handle; and it conducts heat to the same area. And if you see that [the navel area] is closed, then make a closed candle holder, and have the instruments full of oil to purify the head; and have one hand to hold the instrument when heating the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the skin
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	The shoulder often becomes diseased and grows so large that it can be seen, and it must be operated on at the beginning, removing all of its flesh. Then apply a cauter or burning medicine to it; and if you delay surgery until it is large, be aware if it has become hardened, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure substance, not of bad color, and you can see that you can completely remove it, the patient will feel empty and safe, and the wound will heal quickly and tightly.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the flesh is cut out
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuance comes into one of these worked cartilages, it brings little profit, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to do what happens in some men, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips at a suture, then heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are already dried out on one side and the other, you must scrape off all the parts of their skin as long as they are healing, then assemble the two lips at a suture, bind it, and powder on dragon's blood powder, and incense powder; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster of strong glue or another binding plaster, and let it be until it cools by itself, then heal with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of stitching is that you assemble the cut: with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I told you earlier.
des apostemes des levres	Les apôtèmes des lèvres se présentent souvent sous la forme de tumeurs ou de bourgeons qui poussent sur les lèvres, en particulier après une blessure ou une irritation. Ils peuvent être douloureux et peut même gêner la fermeture des lèvres.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A multitude of people have a hard abscess inside the lips, similar to grains of millet, and smaller and larger ones. Then you must turn back the lips, and split them in each part, and take it as tweezers and press into each part; then fill the place after the vitriol incision, so that the blood is stopped; and then remove the scab, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the skin of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there appears on the gums a swollen skin, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let it bleed or dry; then put on the place vitriol paste, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that skin returns after the incision, and appears many times, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are times when they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and there are times when the tooth is black and green and worm-eaten, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks. Then it is necessary for you to sit the ailing person in your hands, and their feet should be in your sanctuary, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, as long as there remains nothing; and do the same with the blackness and greenishness, and the yellowness and other blemishes, until they are cleansed. And if you take out what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to the work that the instrument shows, because the rasor with which one removes the teeth outside has other forms than those with which one removes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can to extract it, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, so that there should be no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to urinate, it behooves you to be certain about the urine.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient fades and they believe it is the urine of Saint, and they make them urinate the good urine; and notwithstanding the pain does not depart by this means, until the bad humour leaves, for we have already seen this happen to those saints; and when you are well certain about the urine, it behooves you that you scrape all around the tooth on every side, with a sharp instrument so as to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your hands or fine pincers in a small space, until they are well extracted, then tighten the pincers; and have the patient's leg in your hand between your knees, and hold tight so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards extract the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and then move it just as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is pierced and infected, you should fill it with cloths, in the place where the perforation is; and if it is strained gently with tweezers so that it does not break when straining; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and report to the patient by the wickedness of the root greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in the same way as foolish physicians who, through haste and boldness, sometimes break the tooth and do not bring about what we have described; but sometimes bring about great illness by the roots remaining or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with vinegar or ash and oil; and if there is bleeding there comes, which often happens, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one must draw out the tooth first, should be long-pointed and have large handles, so that they do not double back when you pull on the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have thick handles so that they do not bend when being pulled, and be well-made of iron and have teeth to hold the wire.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place on the other side, then you must put moistened cotton or bread on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the place is softened, you can insert the forceps called "algefri", by which the joint seems to be bitten like a saw; and they are made inside in the same way as a file and this shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all the pincers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", which is to say a palinche (a type of drill or burr), whose shape is this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good. If not, you should help with all the instruments, whose shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one needs help from this instrument which has two handles, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fasteners that are in front in proportion to the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pincers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be for breaking, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise and subtle masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases in which the ancients did not teach a single instrument due to the diversity of cases, and one does not break the bone or other bones, unless they look for instruments as I have said, and help from gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding for holding the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of medicine suitable to this case, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then reap everything with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape, and its form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then scrape it. And if it is crowded with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the shape, and it resembles a small beak, and it should be made of iron with a sharp tip on top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file is rough and rough in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you cannot move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, take a file of this kind, of which this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also how one makes needles; and in sharpening the point of a tooth, one does so gradually, little by little, so that it does not move until it becomes sharp; then the plane smooths it at the end to be completely flat, and if the teeth are too sharp and they wound the tongue, one must hone the roughness so that it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth knocks loose, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press down on it without spitting it out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, and these do not work; then you must bind it with a thread of gold, because threads of silver become green and rot, but gold does not change; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the tooth being directed towards the healthy tooth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth between the other teeth, if there is one or more, until you come out to the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand skillfully and carefully, until it does not move anymore; and keep a ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the bones of the thread and hold them in pincers, and assemble them, and point them between the healthy tooth, and put them so that they do not hurt the tongue; and then let it stay tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, if it is bound with another string; if it remains and will serve thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the direction of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one must put it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and let nobody who is not wise and patient interfere with it; and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from an ox's rib, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it just as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to clip the thread to the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At any time this string comes from under the tongue or natured, that one is born thus; or by accidental wound healed; and the works are such as you work on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your healthy tooth, and lift up the tongue; then take the nervous string of the large, so long as the tongue is disjoined from its seat, and if there is stiffness or knot, and it is due to a wound healed suddenly, if one puts the styptic and takes the large that binding; and be sure that the tear is not too deep down for the artery which is under; and when you have done this, then lift up the water of rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, and put under the tongue a cloth of linen; and bathe the patient each night, so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the decoration of blood comes, then put vinegar on the place; and if the blood flows, then cauterize with a slow fire, which is good for this; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is green or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards the navel, and there is moisture, make an incision, and the lance it, and make a fine spatula, and deliver it from one part and from another; and if the pus goes to your work, put vinegar powder on top until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have removed all the fluid; then lift the abscess with oil and silk, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	At times comes within the throat pouches that are called "godath", and they are properly called the "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and of fusse colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the decoration of blood; but let it be until it dies, and then you will cut it out, or else it would break apart on its own; and if it is of white colour again, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument to saw, but first look whether the abscess has grown calm and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his eyes should be covered with a cloth, and one should open the mouth and take hold of the tongue between the hands, and press the tongue down on all the instrument, by which this is done; and it should be made of silver or refined gold just like scissors:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the swelling, then take the forceps and stick it into the almond, and pull it out above as far as you can; and remove any threads with it, then cauterize at the instrument, of which this is the shape, which looks like a hook; and although the end is curved, one place to another, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument handy, then cauterize with pincers, of which this shape is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be cut on one side, and on the other named; and when you have cut out one of the almonds, if you cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot, sharp, and soothing water, and they cease to bleed, then gargle the patient with water or the rinds of lemons are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then cure them as long as they are sound; and sometimes other swellings arise in the throat than the two almonds, if you cut them in the same way as the two almonds agree.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside the throat, namely the abscess of small sense; and I had well closed all the throat, so that the woman could not exhale because the conduit was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus in one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that I had put two poultices through each of the two openings of the birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and I inserted the catheter in one opening, then the tube burst and a large portion of pus came out; then I reinserted it into the other opening of the birth, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I inserted the catheter into the abscess, and drained part of it, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus was blocked the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting away at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the place that I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I drained it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and knew only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	Il semble que tu aies ajouté une ligne de texte qui n'est pas liée à la traduction du texte original. "De l'uve" peut être un terme médical ancien, mais sans plus de contexte, il est difficile de savoir ce que cela signifie.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein swells up at the elbow, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a lump and rounded, it is called "vein".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the suppurating abscess has been calmed down, and it is subtle, then you must lance it; and that one which is rounded together and is not long; and it is bloody or of foul color or black, then you must avoid making an incision into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument about which we have made a reminder before; then insert the needle into the vein, and draw it out below, and lance at the places of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too far beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more than that, you will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and heal it until it is sound.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear from cutting, then you should use an expedient in the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauter is hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your vein, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and mix with hot iron filings, so that they are not too thick nor too clear; and take the handle of this instrument, by which it is shaped.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take the chief a comb of hair or put ointment on it, as the men do with a spoon, and put the instrument over all the ointment on the eye; and have the patient sit beside you so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat or the wound. Then hold your hand over all the ointment and press on the eye with the quantity of a half hour until you see it turn dark brown and the medication's irritation is calmed; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the hollow of the eye up to the point that the cotton touches the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete. Then let it dry and wait four or five days.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than incision or cautery; if it is treated by smoke according to this manner: take calamus and yarrow and origanum and rue and camomile and hawthorn and similar herbs, and put all or some of them together in one pot, and I heat it up; and the pot be well glazed with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is silver or lead, and one of the pieces is thrust into the patient's mouth as long as the vapour rises to the eye by the cord, as long as the eye is deadened; then it starts again often, as long as the eye dries, and be careful that you do not do this at the beginning of the rising of hot abscess, for many things occur there; and do not do this except in the decline of hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut. li chapistres des apostemes	It seems like we have gone from a medical text to a diagram or illustration!
