Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, then, what happens after the mucus has been stirred up, judge from that what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be cleansed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then lay him on his back, on something high, and put much cloth underneath him; then sit next to him and instruct the minister that he sits on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two corners of the groin; then take the spatula left, and scrape the skin of the groin in the middle up to the navel, and let the incision be entirely straight cutting the skin of the groin just until it turns white, and peel it subtly according to our power; then pierce the skin plain with water to a large hole, and draw out all the water, and then put stitches, and bind the skin together; and do not touch the groin itself, but let the skin alone; scrape entirely or by pieces similarly the corner of him subtly, so that if you do not scrape it well skillfully, the water will return; and if the urine bursts forth at your work, then gather it in its place when you have completed the work of the skin; then assemble the two leaves of the groin to a suture, then cure it just like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the uterus corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended in doubt of bleeding; then scrape the cervix to the entire suspension, and extract the uterus, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the tendon is joined together in two parts together, know that they are two strings; take the other part so as you have made the first even, then squeeze out the blood, and put a damp cloth in oil rose on the wound; and put outside another damp cloth in wine and oil, and put above two cushions, and above double cloths, and bind it up with all the thread which is according to this shape.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and stuff them with chopped wool according to this shape and be sewn together in the neck of the breeches, and one end takes up from the fundament down to the back, and the other at the part of the elbow; and the other two ends above the two armpits, and so that everything is assembled into the bandage of the breeches; and sometimes this cord of cautery in place of iron cutting is medicined, and it is that you take a subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the buttocks, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scab that contains the tendon is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this shape, and pierce that scab with little holes, and scrape with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the poultice in all ways that you can, as long as you exhaust everything; and be careful that fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is more safe; and beware of bleeding of blood, and beware of the works of cutting; and if nothing contraries you, or swelling of abscess or bleeding of blood or another thing, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horribleness, then instruct him in perforation, as I told you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs which we have said that a fistula is there, then make the patient sit on a high seat; pierce the abscess at the part underneath up to the whole thickness, and put the perforation of long length through the body; and be wide the hole, so that all the water may flow out; then place cotton on the place, and bind it, and let the remaining water run out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out in the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument by which they treat the water of dropsy, whose shape was shown before; and expand the pouch of the wound, and know that the water will return, and will assemble itself after six months or about it, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	The end of the text! It appears to be a medieval medical text, likely from the 15th or 16th century, dealing with the treatment of an aposteme (a type of boil or abscess) in the scrotum. The text provides detailed instructions for diagnosing and treating the condition, including surgical procedures and post-operative care.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Be aware that in the cutting of this branch there are many fears and preparations, for which it seems to me more worthy to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many apostenmes come to the body, and indeed the scrotum; and it is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by superfluity of bitter and sharp water that has spread to the groin, or through percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it finds no pain, and the abscess is heavy; and by chance there are heavy and hard abscesses, and of bad color, and sometimes comes from a bursting artery, or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a bursting artery, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fists; and it does not seem right that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from an inflamed vein is known by the arrangement at the expression of the touch with your fists, and you can very well make a cut above this likeness, and on the other sinews; and it is that you cut the core of the groin, then lift the testicle up high, and cut the white sheath, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the calf is already swelled with these boils or pimples, then you must draw out the blood, and the pus; and if it is hot to the syphilis, or within the blisters, then you must deliver all that swelling, and the pus again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birthmark is near the back, then it is necessary that you cut out all of it, and extract the sac, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are completed, you should dress the wound with damp wool in rose oil and wine, then apply other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	The end of the text! It appears to be a medieval medical text, likely from the 15th or 16th century, dealing with the treatment of an aposteme (a type of boil or abscess) in the scrotum. The text provides detailed instructions for diagnosing and treating the condition, including surgical procedures and post-operative care.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a swelling enclosed in an enveloping membrane like a bladder, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient feels great pain when he urinates; and the treatment for this disease is also very fearful, as was mentioned before, and nonetheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you have the patient sit on the high stool, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your shoulders, up to all the vessels that are close to the penis, and tie them tightly, and stretch them out; then cut with a sharp knife wide at the intersection of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scorch from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first point where the pulse came, and tie it again to the other head; then cut straight down through the middle, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted vessels; then treat the wound as you do with others who have an abscessed navel, so that none of the vessels may bleed which nourish one of the testicles; for if all the vessels come into view, it is necessary to cut out the testicles at all the vessels; so that the body does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and wither and cannot help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	of the twisting of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this rash are by the section that comes out from the spleen, or by extending on the belly in the part of the groin, because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the sides; and this rupture is either from a bursting spleen, or from an extension of it, and these two kinds of movement come from: either percussion, or jumping, or vomiting, or lifting a heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is from extending of the spleen, are that it has puffing and pitting, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and the swellings are even up to towards the deepest part, because the spleen presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the incision of the spleen, that a sudden pain comes at the beginning, and the abscess appears in different forms under the skin nearby, because of the issue of the intestine and the body from the far part of the spleen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at all times they [the intestines] descend with the spleen and are retained in that way, and cause great pain to suffer the sick person, especially when it is compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And with these treatments of iron powder to pour on [the wound], why does he take the risk to recover?
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	The way to operate is that you command the patient to draw the intestine into his hand inside the wound, if it can enter; then have him be seated on your lap between your hands, and lift up his knees; then stretch out the skin of the scrotum upwards, and scrape off all the skin of the sides long-wise; then insert threads from the bandage into the layers of the abdomen as you need to open the wound, so that the opening can be made for the eye to come out; then peel off the spleen that is under the skin of the scrotum, until the white spleen core is uncovered all around; then put your index finger in what is next to the testicle, between the white spleen core which is under the skin of the egg and between the second spleen core, and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second spleen core; and then move your right hand inside the scrotum, and stretch out the white spleen core upwards into your left hand, and lift up the egg with all its surrounding spleen towards the abdomen; and command the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and untie what is behind it beyond the ligation; and test with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine entwined around the white spleen core, and if you find anything, put it into the belly under; then take a needle that has four threads made from ten threads, and insert it in the back part of the spleen, which is after the skin of the scrotum; after the testicles, then scrape off the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads; then assemble one thread on top of another in the shape of a cross, and tie up the spleen, about which we have spoken that it is under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong ligation of two parts; then entwine the threads of the testicles, and tie them up firmly with two parts, so that no blood vessels that nourish them can enter in, lest an abscess form; and then put back again the ligation according to the first long ligature of a span between you and it, and after these two ligatures leave the spleen which is under the skin of the scrotum as large as your index finger; and then do the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then scrape in the part that is under the skin of the scrotum, until the sinewy cord comes out, as we have said before; then anoint with ointment-soaked wool and put it on wounds, and I will bring the ligation which we have spoken.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white skin that we have said to cauterize after the incision, due to fear of blood discharging.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For it happens often, and leave the ligature until it takes hold by itself; and if he tarries to fall, then be rinsed with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it takes hold; then treat the wound with another cure, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	It looks like we've moved on to a new topic.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	I am never seen a person who dared to make the treatment by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made in the same way as the reed which is bound around the stick, in such a manner that you bind the ligaments, after cutting above them slightly beneath; then split it in two, and treat the abscess of those who suffer, until the ligaments drop; and then cure it in the way we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes comes rupture in the abscesses, as we have said, and opens the place; and do not let any of the intestines protrude to the crotch, and if they do protrude, it is a sign, and repair all hours; and nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, the wound or abscess swells, until the intestine protrudes; and this happens through the extension of the abscess which is in the abscesses, as we have said, for it is stretched, then becomes softened and swollen the place and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the rupture from large to small according to the size of three fingers; and then extract the abscess which is under the skin that follows, then take the thread and place it on the apparent swelling of the abscess; and press it deeply into the belly, then sew together the two swellings apparent of the abscess on the end of the thread, and sew one and the other; then extract the end of the thread, and do not cut the abscess nor stretch the gut or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the reed of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hairs, instruct the patient to let the wound remain undisturbed and cured until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syrup is thickened, and has no appearance in the texture, and the cautery is most beneficial in this place, and more close to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from softening of the skin of the groin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the groin is often softened in certain men, because the veins inside them are made soft, and it can be seen; and when you want to treat it, you make the patient lie on their back, and cut out the softened skin from over the natural skin; then sew together the two lips with a suture, and if you see fit, sew first the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches tightly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the flagellation (or whipping)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me that I did not speak of it in this book; and there is no need to mention it except for two reasons: one, so that the barber may know how to respond when asked about it and its treatment; and the other, because we often have need to castrate certain beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: or by attraction, or by tearing open.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then taking them in your hand, as long as they remain soft and you no longer feel anything.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The punishment of branding: it is necessary that you brand the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike on each eye with a hammer when you have well scraped them; and leave no fat or subtle fat which is above the vessels; and this manner of punishment is more gentle than that which is made by attraction, for in attraction something from the testicles remains by chance, because of which the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	La matière de ces hermophrodites est tres obscure et tres difficile a traiter, car il ne sont pas des hommes, ny des femmes, mais les parties de l'un et l'autre se trouvent en eux.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two manners among men: one of which is that between the two testicles appears as well as the shape of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes they urinate through the genitals.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the navel as well as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment of the boil and the swelling is that you close all the closed sores, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men from whom the urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	The tenthigenie (a reference to Theophrastus' Characters or possibly an error)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tentigo is a closed sore on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have as big one as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you stain the superfluity of the tentigo with your hand or nails, and close it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest bleeding occurs, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and a another sore that arises at the mouth of the nipple, and attach an instrument, and by chance bursts forth, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for this reason they called it the ancient "maladie kowee".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you bind it, as we have said of the treatment, and cure until it is healed.
de erratique	La description semble être un texte médical ancien, possible du Moyen Âge ou de la Renaissance.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic disease is when the nature of the woman is not clear, or the womb is small; and it occurs by birth, or accident from illness that has come; or it is caused by a thick thread, or fine or dense tissue, and it is done inside in the uterus, or in the sides, or under, or wherever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly having flowers; and knowledge of this is by looking at the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is close and apparent, it should be on your shoulders or back.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a fine thread and it is close to the two kidneys, then hurry, and sew it in: put your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then hold the two kidneys firmly, until the fine thread comes out, and you will see the swelling; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and place it on the wound, and keep the woman at home each day, so that she cannot sew.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the splint is hard and thick, it is necessary that you apply the poultice to the spatula resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swellings are of flesh, suspend it to the armpit and apply poultice; and have medicines that congeal blood, such as aloe, dragon's blood, frankincense, and egg together in abundance; then attach a strip of linen broad so that the wound cannot heal; and thus be long-lasting, and then provide a tent of dry linen; then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the breast comes flesh, it is necessary to cover according to this manner, unless it is an enchanted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the enchanted abscess which is in the breast, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorrhoids are openings of veins without a customary skin covering, and when hemorrhoids are old they become fibrous; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and fibrosis, when they are deeply in the arse and do not appear to feel, there is no cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the arse, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then set the fibroid on the tongs and burn its roots, then powder over medicine restraining blood, such as aloe and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet with a cold poultice for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the bleeding stops, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and aloe, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he holds still, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him take cupping glasses on the back and shoulders without hurting them; then take linen, and moisten it with juice of plantain or with juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled, so treat the place with ointment until they are healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a sharp headache, then it should be covered as I said earlier; and then treat them until they are healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Les apostèmes de la marris (rectum) ! C'est un sujet sensible, mais je vais essayer de fournir une traduction et des informations utiles.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess come to the buttocks, such as ulcers and stony abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes to the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that collect pus; and if you want to know how to treat iron (i.e. cauterize), look and see if the abscess is swollen at its beginning of appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce (it), but let it cool down as long as the pain is alleviated; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and hold two small seats or he reclines in them, and lean on his back and assemble his feet at the opposite side of the leg; and have his thighs spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then insert the tool towards the right side, and it brings the instrument by which one operates the mouth of the groin, of which this form comes later; and it is necessary that when you bring in this instrument, you insert the pointed part first to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary to place the nozzle of the instrument above, and to hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess bursts and it is treated with soft cloth, then you should cover the head of it at the suture site. And when the bladder is empty, you should put wet cloths soaked in rose oil or green tea into the wound; and place the wet cloth at the bottom of the bed, and place a netted woolen compress above the bed and on the elbow; then cure after two days of ointment coming to what they are supposed to do, until it is healed. And sometimes take away the compress and the wound by a wash with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and aristologe long cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in a bed, then you should beware of cooking with iron, but heal it just as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Je vous ai mal compris ! Vous voulez que je traduise le texte médical en anglais moderne, n'est-ce pas ? Désolé pour la confusion !
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first at the bedside that she know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are such that when you see the woman hasten to descend below, and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out with force; then you should know that this childbearing is according to the natural figure, and the issue comes out under its head, and the placenta with it; and when you see these signs, you should press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends above its head, the placenta comes out with it, and the mother is freed of her superfluities by good purification; and this which comes out otherwise does not come out naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes out under its feet, and forces itself out of the body or head, and hands, or it comes out under her belly, or sideways, and is converted by chance over its neck, and by other evil shapes; so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out through its head by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtues of the child are weak, make her sit on a stool, or have the women hold her; and prepare an oil or fenugreek paste that has been cooked, and then have the midwife give it to her between her teeth as a small spatula.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And tear open the secondine, and cut at her finger nail as far as the moisture that is inside can go; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must have the woman take a purging draught of fenugreek with sesame oil; then have her press and strain on her condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child should be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands are far up, you should have them gently ease in a little by little; and if they cannot get in, lay the woman on the delivery stool, and lift her feet high; then drop the stool to the ground, and keep the woman from standing; and if the hands cannot get in and the child is dead, cut the hands with the scissors that are put there before, and extract the child, and ease them back into place.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up onto its feet, you should push it upwards; and then turn it back and forth little by little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps just to its thighs, he should command it to stop, and make it stifle its crying; if it jumps high, then may God want.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't straighten out like we've said, then turn it slowly and carefully, until it is in its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is loose again.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take muscillage of almonds, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the natural moisture of the woman inside and above this ointment, then make her sit in a warm bath up to the armpits; and when she is moistened underneath, then bind a belt of myrrh around it, and place it under, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her stifle her crying and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press the belly, because now the child jumps.

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement. de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes none are born three or four; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often enough.

de plusors enfans	of multiple children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than that up to XV, and are altogether shaped like an infant by the measurement of a wise and glorious size, and it is necessary that the surgeon knows all these things, because similar things may happen; so do according to what it is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marriage back to its place

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (meaning: to insert something into the anus)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle skin flap: so then the nurse must cause her to pierce that skin flap with an awl at its due place, and let her not pierce through spatula-edged needles, and secure the lacing so that she does not touch it; then put on linen soaked in vinegar and oil, then apply ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it won't close again, then put or insert a plug of linen, and let it stay for a while, and be removed when the baby wants to go into the chambers (meaning: when the baby is born).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And any time this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary to close that sudden opening: if it is cured, as we have said of the linen plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	about the fistula in the fundament (meaning: anal fistula)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are called nodation, and grow larger than those that come from below the fundament forward, or in the separation of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it works, and increases with moisture from a white or subtle boil, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and are known by the fact that they secrete or eject pus or gas when the patient makes an effort to expel them, and perhaps spit up worms.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the join of the thigh, and just to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula that pierces to the fundament and does not pierce: and it is that you thrust your finger or index into the fundament, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula where there is tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, you insert a thin awl or the hair of a horse until you feel the awl or hair with your thumb; and if you don't feel it, nor does the purulence, vomiting, or discharge come out as we have said: know that it does not pierce; if you hurry to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent right up to the bladder or to the channel of urine, if it causes the urine to flow out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces just to the joint of the crotch, then the discharge comes out just to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then know that it will go away on its own, and there's no use in medicine or ointment by anointing; and in piercing fistulas there is no strong cure except purging, and the vanity of foolish physicians who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient. Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes are fistulas formed in this manner: and it is when you pierce the tent into the fistula, and it is on the opposite side of the foundation near the skin above, then take a punctured tent at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I insert one thread in two, and insert the probe into all the thread in the fistula as far as its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced on the edge of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that puncture, in the same way you pierce your nail or the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for one day or two; and restrain it sometimes, until the threads bind themselves between the two, and discharge; then cure the wound until it is sown and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then have it pierced in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not seem fitting to cover the wound if it is that deep inside, and then have it healed, as we said, until it is completely sound.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinal thorn from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and serrated; and on the other side it is not, because of this one does not bind what one should not bind, as you see here:
des emorroydes	bleedings
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Swollen lymph nodes are according to II manners: or they are inside the fundament, like resin seeds, and there are small and great ones, and in cortex always blood, and there is one or more of them, and they are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have much moisture, and in cortex always a little drop of citrine water or a little drop of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure for these who have them inside the fundament, is that you command the patient to sweat so he may go into chambers, until the fundament lets him go outside, and the son appears; if it is urgent, and the patient has a fever, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut off in its roots; and if the lymph nodes cannot be held because of their moisture, take them up on a cloth, or cotton, or from a piece of camlet; and take them out at your two hands, then cut them, and powder above some hot powders that are instead of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure with other cures until they be healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then purge the patient with a purging catheter and sharp for washing what is inside the fundament so that it may come out clearly; when the patient takes hold, and the string are outside the fundament, then is the cure easy; and it is that you take them at your fingernail or at tenailles, and cut them, then cure as we have said, until they be healed, and that he fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must bring the needle according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, so that they are thick; and hold the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one at the top to collect excess blood; then put on the bottom a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or ceruse, and put it on the fundament, and command the patient to rest; and then let him be until he urinates, and when they will have dropped, cure them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the scabbing of the flesh or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is scabbing of the flesh in the intestine, and due to constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must resurface to the tip of a splinter or at your nail the outer layer, which does not let it get moist; then cure it until it is solid as it should be; and if it cannot dry, then re-scrape it more strongly than before, so that it heals well, and becomes scabbed; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of or about a boil (or abscess)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small, false appearance near the body, and go very deep inside; and sometimes they find the frost, and feel it just like dead from trembling, and come into the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose, or a strong fowl's feather, and put that quill on the swelling, so long as the purple circles surround the swelling all around; then turn your hand completely around the whole quill so you cover the entire swelling, and put it very deep, and draw out the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make a thread of copper or iron in this shape, and be subtle underneath and twisted on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that the heat may hold to the inside, and squeeze it And if you wish, scorch or cauterize the boil with a hot iron, as it is done in front of a cauterizer's shop.
de la forme dou clistere	in the shape of a catheter (or syringe)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times one makes a catheter of silver or gold, or melted copper or maillet (a type of metal), and at times one makes these instruments small and large, according to the use for which they are made.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small and large catheter is as above, with a wide head or mouth, or the belly (or bulb) is joined in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is an obstruction or the belly is bound together, as you see, and the head of the stomach is pierced inside; and has two holes on one side, and in the other one; and the belly is filled with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there are ten spaces between each hole, then put into these holes a strong thread made of twisted rough yarn in an X shape or about it, and gather the belly together like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, bind it up before with a strong thread, then purge; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or goose fat or something similar, then put it in lightly; then have the servants hold the blister with both hands together until it is completely dry, then take out the blister, and lift the patient's legs high up, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it go that long as it can; and if the patient sleeps all night straight away, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize in the disease of obstipation or constipation of the belly, and the medicine comes out quickly, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in their foundation or abscess, then let the blister be as subtle as for a child; and it is the shape of the subtle blister on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatment of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and with what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by stoning and the cutting of sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or breast, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn completely and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hot abscess: if so, cleanse it immediately with cephalic solution, even if there is pus coming from the wound, and let the wine and thick meats fill the patient.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, then let its meat be diminished, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, moist cotton in rose oil only, or in vinigared wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, powder that I will say about later; and if the burn has moved it, then put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar thing, and the edges cannot be closed by stitches, then close them with sutures, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and festers, and only holds together with a small amount of skin, then scrape it off; next cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard tissue in place of soft skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meat, such as roasted testicles and wheat bread, also fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a putrid skin infection, and it does not reach the bone, then scrape off all the pus, and discharge it, next cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with medicines, then cut out the artery; and if you can't loosen it, tie it with a thread; and if that doesn't help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it's that you put on this powder which soothes as soon as the scab has formed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take one part incense; blood of dragon two parts; and living gall three parts, and powder it finely, and apply the wound tightly, so that it becomes well-sealed and joins all its blood; and then bind it well, and let it be unbound if it swells; for one does not remove medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with just chalk alone, when there is not incense nor blood of dragon, but only after the scab has formed on the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, itself being in its place, then do not put on this powder at all; but apply some digested ointments, or flour made from barley dough mixed with water and honey, as long as it discharges pus; then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then draw it out with fine tweezers; and I will tell you afterwards about breaks of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a boil, then there should be no other treatment than to let the cure happen, and not put on any constricting thing, because it harms boils and makes them shrink; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of boils is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the most high member; but if the medicine is strong, such as hazel bark dissolved in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water, and other stones like this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up with stitches and tie it with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and wide and full of pus, then pierce or further down from below; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and tie, and cauterize as needed; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is guarded, so that the meat goes, then sew up the wound on the dog's neck, but do not touch the throat, but place it according to its natural shape; and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments of detestable herbs until they are healed; and if the wound has caused impression in the bone, then scrape it; and if there is pieces of bone, then take them all out if you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound festers, and dries up, and closes the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
