Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look if there is wind-bursting coming out of the wound in front of the patient: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at the first hour nor bind it because the blood will not stop flowing into the depth, and it will return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound three days, or four, or more; then there will not come spasms, nor evil trembling of the heart nor convulsions from the brain; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with poultices and other treatments until it is sound; and if it cannot heal, and work, know that there is a fistula; treat it thus as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse on the back, treat that which is in front with an ointment; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has broken into the bone, and there are splintered pieces, close the wound, and let loose the stitches if they are tied up; and if not, let the wound rot, so that the extractions will be lighter; and for other wounds on other limbs judge thus as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are great and medium and small; from the large wound intestines sometimes burst out or the membranes of the intestines through which their introduction takes place; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it's worse than a small wound that a great one, for this reason we insert the intestines in slowly, if we don't put them in hot to hot; because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, so they go back inside slower, and for this reason it's better to make a medium-sized incision, for this reason we reset the intestine to its place rather than others two And know that the rupture of the belly is according to 4 ways: the 2 common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body and 2 other proper stitches are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and no part of the intestines protrudes, and a gentle thing must be put back in place, this can be done by one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a wool cloth in hot water only, or cook it in boiling water with squill and cypress and spike, and wrap the intestine until the swelling is removed; and once you have done this, strain it and it will be sufficient to unswell.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine in water or boil ale and onions, because by this means the opening is freed from something; and if it cannot enter, make a pouch for the wound with an instrument with which we lance boils; and the first cure is to cut, that none of us should cut without great necessity having been there; and that is the instrument to split it: if you cut inside in the curvature and not outside, and look at this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines have burst forth, so place them back in their natural form according to their proper place, if you are able, for this will be advantageous.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the part under the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part under the belly, place the head and the hips higher than the parts below, and also as for the rupture of the belly in one of its two parts, place your attention so that the injured part be higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to take note of what I say about big and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, place what you can over them, then take a seamstress's needle that reaches all along the rupture to its end, and bring together the edges; and this is the common method of sewing, and it is to take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound's breadth, then leave the head of the wound at about two finger-widths' space, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the four corners of the skin with the two corners of the siphac, which is inside the skin, until you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the siphac in one seam; then pull tight a double-threaded string around the needle from two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound properly, and then leave about two finger-widths' space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do this with the needles, until all the wound is closed; and have the needles average in size, between fine and coarse, for fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and too coarse ones cannot well enter: therefore it should be average; and it does not need to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the seam is formed; then pull out the needle tips, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and I place threads or cloths on the needle tips for a means of holding them, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this method of sewing with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices to use one needle or two, The second suture is common, and it is that you bring together the four corners of the skin and the four corners of the siphac in a single needle where there is a strong middle thread; and when you have pierced these four corners altogether, then draw out the needle from the part where you began, in the manner one sews clothes; and leave about two finger-widths' space between each seam; this stitch men know, and I sewed up a wound that had been on a man's belly, which was hurt by a knife, and the wound was over a palm's length wide, and it reached into the intestines well over two palms in width, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to him the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours; and the wound was healed in just 15 days, and I cured him, and he became sound.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in this place where there is none found, nor any medicine; and I put clean cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he became sound.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle, and push it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced through right in front of each other, then turn the thread of the suture or the sewing thread where you pushed the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew as the pelt makers do with pelts, and you leave once the thread on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which the Greeks call properly, is such that some do: they assemble the two parts together naturally and apply one end of the suture to the other end in this way: place a needle or pointed instrument close by and make it pierce only that place; then leave the two ends of the suture. Then turn the needle and have it pierce from the outside part to the inside part, at the two ends of the suture. Then have one and the other pierced from the outside part to the inside part, in two other holes of the mirror which are on the other side; and this is the manner of sewing that is more proper and most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this word and some testify it: one must sew the belly with two needles, or thread in each; and you should put one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets. And know that when a tear is within the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the fire has changed it, so remove the intestine and the fat; then put on powdered quick charcoal, and if the fire has changed it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and clean the threads, and sew up the skin and the flesh; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, so put on, just as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause community among the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten light linen with tempered hot oil or rosed oil and put it around the angles and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or purulence in the intestines and many times occurs, so cleanse them with black wine vinegar and similarly if the purulence comes just to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines that are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and this is because of the firmness of their vessels, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon leaps out of the wound, so return it behind, as with the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must bind the place that is black, so that bleeding does not occur there, because there are vessels and arteries; then sew up what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends of the limb from the part under the wound all the way to the outside in order to lighten the extraction when the tendon falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the tear of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen one man injured by a lance to the stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and was sewn up and became a fistula, and there came out feces and flatulence from it; I applied treatment according to what I could do, and did not cease to subtilize until he was healed, and the place was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sew it, I doubted that the patient would have evil in his belly; and there was no evil, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he should be bound thus: take worms from great testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the worm has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips, so that they squeeze their mouths together; and then strike the head, and this holds so that he cannot undo it, then put another worm after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and that closes the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That head is sewn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that has been cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the end of this thread of intestine that is quite loose, and then tie it with the top of this thin linen thread twisted together, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and straighten out the stitches; and this method of sewing with worms is no different from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the rounded intestines, there is neither remedy nor healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is commonly called a "fistula"; and similarly when it is swollen and spreads downwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the true nodation [?], that is hard and white, or where one does not feel pain, and it is also swollen like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it breaks out downwards, and sometimes becomes thick; sometimes dry, and sometimes quite wet; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is solely because of one of the nine causes: that is to say, through a lack of blood or strength; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the surface, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is infected, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in its treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or due to the property in the region being slow in digestion, and late in healing, and fleeing by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is fitting that I inform you of the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Abscesses occur in all members of the body; for there are abscesses that come to the major veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so also it comes to the principal property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the abscesses that are in this manner are of grave sanitation, and there is no cure but cutting, and ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come to the place just as I have said, and you have confidence in the treatment, and you know it well, take a tent made of lead or iron, if the abscess is straight, probe it; and if the abscess is twisted, search for it with a subtle tent of cloth, because the cloths bend around the twistiness; and if the abscess has many openings and you cannot probe it well with tents, cleanse it by pressing through one of the openings, because moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then lance the abscess according to your skill, whether there is bone or nerve, and see deeply, and ask the patient very carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and once you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then search for it according to what I have told you, and cut out the badness and corrupted flesh that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the abscess is well found at a straight place, it is necessary that you probe deep, as long as you can, then put moist tents in medicinal water, and fill them up to the head of the abscess, as long as the medicine eats away the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put unguents on raw flesh, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by these means, lanced it just as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the abscess, cut out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not wound or damage the main member, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so extract it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure with things that generate flesh until he is healed; and if he is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you are not going far enough: uncover and scrape as deep as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot come there; since there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course; and if there is a little corrupted bone, and you can pull it with pincers, then extract it with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, do not leave one; and if the moisture causes contractions, and there is no error or fear, then cut and extract the flesh, and deliver the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put a thing with purulent porriture on the wound, and leave it until the leprosy is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily reunited the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, then clear away the corruption only up to where the blackness is completely gone, then close the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupted flesh, and it comes just to the marrow of the bone, you must scrape and cover everything just up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is closed; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was the young man around XXX years old, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the materials came into the leg and there was a large abscess, and he did not have an opening outside to open it; but the surgeons through their foolishness worked on him for so long that they opened the abscess, and much of the material flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there were many holes that all let flow and moist from the body; and many surgeons put treatment around II years, and none wise in the art of hands was there until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what flowed through the holes a great amount; and his whole body became red, and had yellowish-green color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent over one of these ulcers, and then I searched all the ulcers, and found that some were coming against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and I cut into one of the ulcers until I discovered a part of the bone, and it was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption went down to the bone inside; I removed what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there wasn't another corruption, except for the one that I had removed; and I began to heal the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but couldn't sew; and then I re-began, and discovered the bone just as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then thought to sew up the place; but I wasn't able to until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and freed it from all its fibers, then healed it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and sown together, and there was no need to re-start the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who couldn't endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For by the evacuation of blood it often flowed profusely, but it was entirely cleansed, and in place of the bone there formed a hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contraindication at all, nor when he lay down nor when he came.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be reset in this manner: take one thread and strain it to the head of the bone that is open, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and put another thread of linen larger than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, and stay the head so that you draw out the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see fit to reset it, so that the resetting does not harm the flesh; and put a hot coal or a flat stone under the bone to loosen the corrupted flesh; and it must be reset as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and reset again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then lay bare all the flesh. Then put a burning ember underneath, and then sow from one part to another with the corruption, and be sure that the suture is long enough for the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and saw through the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other agent but to cut. And if it is in the hand or foot knuckle, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must ask how it opens; and purify it in all the ways you can, but do not let the vein or nerve be against you; and know that the incisor and the sows for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each similarity of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of illnesses; so consider the instrument which you have need of according to what it requires.
dou feu	from fire (presumably, this is a transition back to the original text, where "du feu" would indicate the use of heat in some way)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints can be injured either inside or outside; and when you have medicated that ulcer with the cure of medicines, and it does not help, you must cover up that member all the way to the place where the ulcer comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the greater malice, which is a fault in the member; and the signs are that the members become black, as if they had been burned with fire, and after the blackness appears, the ulceration of the member spreads to other members and takes hold throughout the body; you must hasten to cover it up, and if it is by the bite of certain venomous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and vipers and similar things, and if the ulcer is in the head of the arm, then cover it, but do not give them any space to come all the way down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes all the way down to the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the ulcer does not come all the way up to the arm; and if it comes on the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtues; and similarly do when the ulcer comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cover after the second joint; and if it comes on the foot, then cover the entire foot; and if it ascends into the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of covering or dressing the member is that you tie it up top and bottom, and extend a servant one of the straps downward, and another servant the other strap upward, and you part the flesh between the two straps an inch wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cover or dress, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the dressing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient with another lesion and swelling.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs from incision comes when you operate, so cauterize the place quickly, or put some restraining powders on it; then come back to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and cure it as long as it becomes whole; and I will tell you what happened to one man in my care: he had a burn that seemed like ash of fire, and that corrosion came first to his heel of the foot, so much so that it took over the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly cauterized the foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned to his heel of the hand, and he came to me, and I put things that would reverberate after the purification of the body on him, and he could not stop the corrosion; and he begged me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of reverberating the matter; and I doubted also that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became desperate completely, and went back to his land, and quickly cauterized his hand, and was healed; and I have told you this solely so that one might do another thing when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Occasionally an abscess appears in the fatty part, and stays for so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; and then they burst and perforate, and the flesh bursts out, as does a wineskin; and the skin which is on top is just as delicate as a fine silk cloth, and do not reach just to the bone, nor just to the nerve, and such sickness is called "sain", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes right up to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that you cut out all around that skin, and meanwhile when it is delicate, just like a silk cloth; and do not sew it back together because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you are certain that the skin has healed, and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cut out a suppurating abscess thus: look if the breast is large, and the tube which comes out of it is of foul odor; then make an Egyptian medicine clister like this: take asafoetida, oil, and larderel, equally, and put the mixture into a vessel over fire, until the medicine becomes red, and becomes just as thick as honey; and then take some of that according to your need, and mix with water and honey, and use it as a clister for the breast, and close the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then squeeze out the water; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and the pus is removed; sometimes a water of ashes is used to clisterize when that medicine is not present, and it's that you take ashes from grape vine wood, and pour water over them, then let it settle, and use it as a clister, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then use a water and honey or there be a small amount of larderel in it; or you use a clister made from honey and sweet wine, which has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the pus to heal; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well cleansed, then use a clister which causes flesh to grow in it, and it's that you take diffinient ointment, and make with rose oil and wine; or you use some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have spoken about treating ointments; and if the opening of the abscess is small, and the tube of the clister cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a piece of iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew up just so that the opening of the clister can enter, and if the tube which comes out of the abscess is above, then cut it lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the breast is in depth, it should not leave hair to grow; and if you cannot cover the chest from below as you see fit, prepare in such a way that the breast sinks to its lowest point, for when the breast is in depth, it should not leave hair to grow and if you cannot cover the chest from below as you see fit, prepare in this manner: so that the breast slowly descends, and let nothing of the breast remain; and take consolidative medicines to put on the chest, and sit above a linen cloth that covers the entire chest; then cut at the strongest point the pustule on the chest which is larger than the first, next smear soft ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the pustule, and put it on the pustule on the breast to ease the breast, and do not remove the large cloth outside that after many days once; and that which is on the pustule on the chest, often take out so as to remove the breast, and know what comes from the breast, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in this manner and you see the nature that emerges on the pustule of the breast, know that the breast has been healed already, and approach health; then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast empties out undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons have coursed after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the healthy are approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is delayed, and those who do the opposite; and if indigestive bile jumps out of the breast after many days, know that the breasts have not healed; and if the breasts delay to heal, and are inflamed, then apply dry medicines with moist substances and dry virtues, such as distilled ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take distilled ointment, and make it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine in substance; then boil and use it; and do the same thing with thickened cooked honey, when distilled ointments are not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and turn into powder on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue a cloth to it, and place it on the breast, and administer long Aristolochia, and roots of heavenly lily, which is also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use simples or composite medicines: grind them up, and make powder, and put it with the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has penetrated deep, and made impression in the bone, or hard members, or tendons; so apply the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the ulcer or sore on the inguen (groin).
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Carbuncle is an abscess that arises beneath the armpit of the hand or foot, or perhaps in other parts; and when it grows old and one does not take care of it, so the abscess bursts and flows and pours pus as long as the root of the ulcer goes; and perhaps it flows all through; and comes a corrosion just to the bone, so painful pain comes, and the holes of the two are wide, and the color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must take a hot iron all around the ulcer and remove all the leftover residue of the ulcer, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the ulcer is sound; but if the ulcer quickly penetrates the flesh, and begins to pierce and tear it, then you must put hot oil under the ulcer where it pierces the flesh and push it up, and carefully and lightly scrape away that flesh, and apply on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and remove it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone marrow is corrupting, then cut into it at the joint in front of the spine just like was said before, then cure it until it heals; and if it is festered and suppurated, and hurts with great pain, then you must first clean it out; then cut the surrounding flesh around the abscess at an angle from top to bottom, and be careful that the knife does not come all the way down to the skin below the abscess, for the patient will feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The tendons that grow in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a bone or it has an angle, and sometimes one grows at the root of the joint, or the origin is in some of the bones of the tendons.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	One who is born in any not or knot of the two digits cannot move, and one who is born at the jointure of the two digits may move; the size of that which is flesh-like is light, similarly: cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that form in the root of the joint are grievous to cure, and you should hold back from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or grows in the rear of the nub, it is necessary that you shave first the flesh around just to the bone, then shave the bone with a string suitable for these things, then sew until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The burn that comes on the hand together comes by birth, or by a blow of a wound, or by being burned with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you shave the suture, so that the wound repairs itself according to its natural form; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so it does not heal; or put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the place is healed, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If burn comes on any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that burn as it is necessary.
des vils	the evil ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swollen veins are large, inflamed, and full of superfluous melancholy substances that come to various limbs of the body; and it more often occurs in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to them no purging of choler, and then heal the wound with basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron (i.e. the cautery) is done in two manners: one is that you scrape and let flow the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and let it flow entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first arise the leg with a hot iron very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned out; then bind the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then scrape the vein at one or two or three places with a wide blade; then raise and let flow the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can endure; and then bind it back up, and instruct them that they should become strong in eating and drinking dark-colored broth; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and be detrimental to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Loose the skin of the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and inflates the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it up over the fire, and then apply a needle to the place where the vein is long at the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then stretch the skin so that it tightens, and peel off the vein from each side until one can feel it; and it is seen red and black, and when it goes into the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the needle under, until it is raised out of the skin, and then pull it to the other needle lightly, then apply it in another place three times; then peel off the skin over the vein so that it appears, then raise it up to the needle, as you have done before, and pull it to another needle, as you have done first; then apply another needle, or more if necessary, then raise it, and cut at the tip of the foot, then stretch and lift just to the second needle; then draw it from one size to another, until it is all free, then cut; and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then insert a needle with a very thick double thread in it, and tie and pull it, and put under the needle, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot pull it or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, then put a moist woolen cloth on the place of the wound in wine and rose oil, and heal it until it is sound.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and curled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it slantwise, but do not close it; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to close the vein is curved and does not pierce, so that it closes the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were subtle, it would pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is situated in the legs, in the hot parts where no herbs or tree grows, and in the earth where there is little moisture; and it may occur elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms grow inside the body, inserted between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this inflammation are such that it comes to the leg a very great redness, then the place changes, and the inflammation begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling opens, you must wrap a piece of linen cloth around it from one and a half to two spans, and tie the knot; and let the linen stay on the leg, and every time it becomes swollen again at the outside, you must rewrap it with the linen, and the knot; and if it is too long, you must cut off part of it, wrap the remaining part in linen, and do not cut it in its root until it is completely out; because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess or corruption at the place, and a bad disease; for this reason it should be treated little by little up to the end, and nothing should remain on the body; and sometimes this swelling is when it is treated of five palms long, or ten, and one came to me once, from whom it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, it puts out pus or a hole, and it empties completely inside, and medicine for preventing corruption every day is applied, then it heals just like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time when the vein is washed clean, and especially when it opens up in a joint of the foot or hand, or there is much pus, and from which it shoots blood; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "the sickness of the bull", because it often occurs in bulls, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body rising and descending, and the person feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and bursts out; and it is generated by the putridity of some humors, such as come worms and serpents and lice and roundworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps entering, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, then one cannot be sure except when it goes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly; then cut on top and draw it out further, and if the worm is deeply lodged in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire on top, until it burns; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head near the eye, then hold a ring under it tightly, then cut on top, and draw it out further; and it is necessary to treat the patient with cleansing of body medicines soluble for evil humors and spoiled meats putridity.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and it can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and I noticed afterwards that it climbed as quickly as an insect on the shoulder, just like living silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain moved away from that place, and was fixed in the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it came into the other arm; then she told me that it kept recurring around the body, as I myself saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness move in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have often seen that pain can move from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman, and I thought that it was because the woman had dry skin, and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason the condition appeared to be caused by bad blood; and they do not notice according to this reason those who are healthy, and who have moist bodies and repaid veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, so bind above and below hastily; and then cut above until the swelling is constrained to its proper place again; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see to your hands, so cure with those who drain swellings, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The types of arrowroot are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they occur.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.
