The diversity of their form is that there are those with large points and small, hairy and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with pieces; and that one which pierces into any member so pierces in two ways: or into the principal member which hangs, such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then into any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, appears to you: if it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in many conditions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the splinter shoots up who is above the brain, is when there is scotoma and sadness and confusion and reversion in themselves, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps comes out through the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice; and shoots from the moist wound a white appearance like pus, and also as if it were a boil of flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then beware of curing, and pull out the arrow unless it is in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow when it pierces the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels as though it were stuck in a hard object not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like the hairs, and there is dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowroot when it never leaves the spleen is that foam comes out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient turns blue, and gasps loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowroot pierces the covering of the spleen, it is located near the lower ribs; and there is a great pain and a great distress and gasping; and all the muscles of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowroot pierces the stomach, perhaps something indigestible comes out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowroot pierces the abdomen and comes out through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrowroot.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowroot pierces the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows away, and the patient feels a great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and hips and knees and calves and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrowroot is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrow pierced the eye in the root of the neck: I attempted it, and led it out on the other side under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had pierced the fat of the eye under the paper of the eyelid, and the arrow was repositioned, and I could not extract anything except the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all made of light iron without ears; the game was healed, and no bad event came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow in the ear; I removed the barbs, and refined it so much that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew out an arrow from the home of a man, who had it stuck in his belly, and thought he was going to die; and then that XXX days passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and bound it, and drew it out, and had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help the man in whose back an arrow fell, and the wound above was sewn up; and the arrow stayed inside him, and did not change his natural conditions, nor found any hurt in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it stayed thus without suffering great pain; and very many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take an arrow out of the side of the king's son, who had been shot into the neck, and it was slightly slanted to the right part; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a fine needle and felt nothing; and he felt pain and discomfort below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on him a plaster that attracts and digests, in order to prevent inflammation at the wound site; and the wound from the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on him for seven days and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this way for a long time, until he felt the arrow itself one day deep inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a medicinal ointment with corrosive properties to the wound by hand every day, until it was fully open, and I tried, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which had hardened at the site; then I introduced into the opening of the wound that medicine ointment, as long as the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and the terminations went well around IV months, and then split so much that I put in forceps, and pulled from one side and the other, and could not come out; then did not cease to subtilize and ingeniously devise with instruments, until I took it one day with good forceps, according to what its form would come at the end of this chapter, as long as I had it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, such that you put your treatment on what I do not say; for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters gather well upon a small thing and upon what is present and deficient, find new work, and a new instrument, at the removal of strange things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs or where they are stuck except in two manners: either through the place where they enter, or on the other side; and the one that goes out from the place where it enters is an arrow entering fleshy parts, and goes out sometimes immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not go out immediately, then leave it so that the flesh around is putrid and the issue becomes inflamed; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for some days and move it each day; and then it goes out, and if it does not, then pierce around it with a very fine needle, until the place around is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent to the patient: do not pull it out, but let it be for a while until it becomes even after some days, because if the arrow comes all the way to the symphac, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not go as far as the symphac, and the patient remains for a while without bad accidents, then it is time to pull out the arrow.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very tightly set in and cannot come out that way, then I administer tar to the area, as I told you before. Then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then look for it with all diligence. And if you can feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument. And if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then clean the wound as much as possible; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it holds, cut away the flesh that is stuck in place from two parts up to where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then let it be until the flesh around the wound has grown over and covered it, then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of incising a nerve or vein, and devise how you may pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid; and if you cannot do so, then put him as shown by the sign.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or if it has pierced anything of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where you see or feel it apparently: cut then above, so far as the tweezers can take hold, and then pull it out; if now it springs forward.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand around strongly, so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and start pulling again as far as it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is inside, then push in the whole shaft; and if the shaft is loose, and you see fit to administer a poultice, then give him the instrument pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is stuck, then insert the instrument with the point entering in, for ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then cure the wound as it needs to.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the lung or liver or belly or bladder or side, and it is nearby, and you can remove from above, if you do remove; and guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which one treats splinters are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and small ones, according to the size of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to stick at the tip of the arrow, as it is this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tweezers for pushing and checking if it fits like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one is cured, of which there are sixteen on the head, to wit: two pipes that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that appear in the two temples; and the two veins that are in the two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is on the crown of the head; and the two gullets that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips at the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: the one is cephalic, and it is located at the left side, and they call the common people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fistula", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it the common people "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call the common people "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and that one from which one bleeds, who opens manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: the one is under the skin of the left side, and the second saphene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called "nates", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins underneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears is very helpful for cathartics and headaches; and the quality of the bloodletting is such as I say to you, which is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a string so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent from the head: that will give you the sign that it works under your hand. Then take the lancet, and insert it behind the vein up to the bone; then raise your hand to the entire vein upwards and cut through the skin and the vein with a pair of tweezers, and let out the blood until you see; then bind and tie it so that it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is worth emigraining anciently, and used, and accustomed, and to the body of the tears sharp as eyes; and the quality of the bleeder so is what I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, until the two veins appear clearly; and feels the hair under his chin, and then signals to cut; then lifts the key above the vein at your index finger, and inserts the lancet below, and lifts the vein upwards, and clips, as you have done in the other two veins, and makes a clot of the blood according to your need; then releases the patient, and puts your finger on the vein for an hour, then puts on cotton; and then closes it firmly, and leaves it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about its clipping and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting from the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraine, and in headache; and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on top of the vein, and press upwards with your hand or something else, and let two drops of blood issue according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein so it is tied and one time the work is done in a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not advisable to make the incisions too sharp, and to bleed across, because the bone is close by, and there is a risk of breaking through the incision if it is too delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the armpits is helpful to the eyes and to scabies, and to headache, and to the erysipelas in the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient strains their neck by twisting from some bond, as before; then bleed them, and let the bloodletting be of a thread, somewhat long of flame, somewhat wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the incision is delicate, it may break through; then make the bleeding stop, as much as you need to, and then tie with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein near the neck is worth a fever, and a tertian fever, and diseases of the face, such as an emigraine and a redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their throat, then strains their neck to your left hand, and takes the thin flame long, and puts it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well itself, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep and make the bleeding of blood according to your necessity, then tie one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two veins is beneficial for the tightening of the intestine, and the beginning of ulceration, and many diseases, and epilepsy, and corrosion, and herpes, and scabies; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their throat under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be on top of the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein from long a little widely, then trail the blood moderately, or as long as it is necessary; then do it again in the other vein, then loosen the ligament, and bind both veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and leave them until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the cleansing of veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding from the veins above the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and redness around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the cleansing of veins is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small dark spots: cut therefore the one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the cleansing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing under the tongue is useful after the cleansing of the cephalic vein, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the cleanser is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein: cleanse therefore one and the other, and do not go too deep because there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat, from which one commonly draws blood, are healed according to two manners: either they prick at all times with a sharp lancet, or olive-green needle so fine as to be called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine in proportion to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the incision is very well known, and it is wide as you see: (description of an instrument or a shape)
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are full of clear blood and contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the shape of the olive-green lancet.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate and pointed, and is for bleeding thin veins where the blood is very clear.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilic, which is one of these veins, serves as a cure for diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him sagaciously, and that he beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows forth, then he must staunch it, as I said; and the lancet should not be pricked, but rather cut like an aseel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open obviously, then you should draw it out and change another one; or you want to drain from it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens obviously; and the copal resin is applied to a flame beforehand, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm, so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with copal resin in the flame; and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: then leave it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flowing upwards just like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is the blood of the artery: hurry then, and put your hand up long, then take your hand away if the bleeding stops, which has happened many times; bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and you are in a hurry, and medical treatment is not available, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will retreat, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig skin and make it into a shape, and take one half and tie it well just above the other; if the blood stops, that's good; if not, cure it with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not grievous in many conditions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bond.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the wrist in the middle so helps that it cures blood from the top of the head and the bottom of the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is below, and if he pokes too deep and finds the nerve, and it swells up and the vein is grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens very often, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must take out the needles from the instrument anesthetically; and push aside the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The wound of the cephalic vein so helps, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed using a flaming olive oil or a flaming myrtle oil, for it is the most safe of all the veins, for it has no artery under the nerve.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Anyway, it is necessary to seek the most gentle position, and do not harm anything if one fails the first time, and try again; and by chance the joints swell in some men when one tries the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that bleeding is not done except to preserve health and to prevent diseases from coming; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are on the neck: it is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours during the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who administers the remedy has no fixed time determined, but when there is need by day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it does not become necessary to heal children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying fruit that is more than three-quarters of a month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly be healed who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever way it is, then it becomes necessary that they open the intestines with a light suppository, if he has much filth retained, so that the veins do not pull out superfluous things harmful to the main members; nor does one heal who is too bloated with meat, or who is drunk, until he is no longer intoxicated, or dropsical; and beware of healing after passion of colic, and vomiting, and defecation of belly, and multiplication of living with woman, and labor, vigilance, and insomnia, and all virtues, or by means of arm or body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thickened, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then enter the bath, if something does not hinder it, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the wound in front of the belly's third part, as we have said; and guard that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the healer be higher than him whom one heals, and wet the arm two times or three, then untie the band above gently, for when it is too tight or loose, so it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the healer's hand with the place where he wants to heal until the veins swell, and are felt; then moisten the healer's flame with an old oil flask, then put his right hand on that wound below the left place where he wants to heal, so that the wound does not catch fire and fail when piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that bleed as quickly as strings being washed in water, and such that are full of windiness, so that when one places the flame on them, they draw back from the flame and cannot be opened; thus is one of these kinds. And if the vein overflows, it is too narrow a wound, therefore it behooves the surgeon to be knowledgeable in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein overflows the first time, it is good; but if not, then he should start again a little below or above that place, unless the skin is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is inflamed and the patient fears it, let him leave it alone for one day or two, and do not tie up the arm: perhaps a bubo will form there. Do not enter the bath, then resume the treatment if you please; and if the opening is small, cut off the blood quickly and quietly, and you doubt whether it's going to be as much blood as you see, so direct the whole flame into that same opening itself; and do this hastily, while the place is inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not restart the incision, and put on a small drop of linseed oil, because it lightens the body of blood, and is mixed with the liquid that the oil is; and thus administer the linseed oil in each incision that you make veins for to stop the flow of blood; and do the same thing for treacle and poultice made from eggs, when put on the place; so soften the skin and separate it when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes which has formed many times, especially when it is not fully purged at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a moist sponge in hot water and warm oil, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has issued from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains on the place after some days, it does not harm him; and if you see fit, put on something made of aloes or myrrh remade in a juice of camphor, mastich, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of badness in the healing of the basilica (a type of wound or swelling), then put your hand on it, and if you find that the place feels soft to the compression of the hand, then it is a sign of badness.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to put any of the things we have said on it, for perhaps it will cut off blood from an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And consider each type of blood according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the blood is black, let it flow out until it turns red; and if it looks thick, let it be thinned out; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is swollen and puffed up, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the incisions be wide; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and let him recover slowly and often, and he must be recovered by cutting obliquely, not by piercing; and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging of blood and severing of nerve, and is more effective than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one to whom the body fails in healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in apple juice; if he is overheated, then apply a poultice of blood three or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, then apply moist bread as a dressing before the healing with a syrup made from honeyed wine, or with aromatic syrup of honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he spits up blood, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he drink a broth of meat and a subtle smelling syrup, and use the other things which we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bloodletting, that he let the body recover a little bit at a time, according to the quantity of his strength continuing.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to straighten his arm after the first bloodletting and he has a strong pulse, will recover in 7 hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be bled on another occasion, must be bled the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already been heated up and caused fever; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the wound as far as it can be pried open; then you will reward all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that death may not come in place of the patient, and this often happens when the bledder is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see him dislodge the arm, and make blood issue a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on it; nor if it is curved, should you stretch out his arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds a second time; or you can prick with the point of the flame, as long as the congealed blood issues from the wound, and put on a piece of string dipped in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let him leave it alone and not bind it at all, until the inflammation has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to let out blood the second time, then he should bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled instead of that of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The manner of the cure is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water, so that the scab becomes red; then it is bandaged moderately, so that the vein appears well, then the wound is now cleaned through [it], not too wide or long; and the skin should be large, and the wound should be cleansed very close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood coagulate in the water, until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the cure of this wound is safer than all other wounds, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure of the swelling on the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the wound is inflamed; if one can see it; and if the blood flows through [the wound], and you take care to clean it entirely, then nothing will be harmed; and do not go too deeply into it, for the nerves are under all uncovered flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the coagulated blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have taken out as much blood as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and thread to sew it up quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding from the hand of the left side is worth the disease of the madmen, and do everything in the same way as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The skin of the soles is equal to all diseases that are under the body, such as the ailments of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the knees and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its skin is that the patient dips his foot in hot water and rubs it on the shin until it cracks, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the shin is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; then cure the largest vein, or at the ankle, which is most valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut into the vein on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut through them also as in cutting; and be careful with the flaps.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the swelling cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well of the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the cure fails the first time, then repeat it the second time above a poultice, because the spot is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so treat the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the knee of fear, and its swelling amounts to the pain of the haunch, when it is by hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health is that the patient enters into hot water, and rinses above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then cleanse it in all ways that you can, and crossing over; and be mindful that you cover him, because the place is safe, and it has been made well known to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then clean the vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make so much clean of the blood as you see, and then untie the string, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	the purifications of a blister (or cupping)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or iron, or glass; and the application of leeches is done in two ways: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosaion which is to be done without fire is in two ways: or it is all at once, or not at once; and the ventosaion which is made by piercing and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places of the body, for one is entirely on the top of the head; and another in the neck; and two others in the sides of the neck; and the ventosaion under the chin; and the ventosas on the shoulders; and the ventosas above the loins; and the ventosas in both arms; and the ventosas in both legs; and the ventosas in both ankles; and the ventosaion does not treat blood, unless it is for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore has not weakened anyone at all, as one makes a bleeding of a vein; and it should not be administered, nor all at once nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to bleed, or for custom, let us bring each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and every time; for there are such who, when they have need to bleed, so have a heavy head; and those who find repletion and redness on their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swollen, and bleeding; and there are such who dream, and see by their blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and all the more so when it's in the middle of the month, let us order to bleed after three hours of day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The purging of the head is so helpful to the weakness of the head... that comes into eyes, and it does not need to be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is in place of the purging of the cephalic vein, and it does not need to be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have catarrh, for it causes them great harm; and therefore it should not be used by the elderly, nor those who have cold head illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, and on this account it is necessary to place the leech a little lower by reason of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosation in the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it is worth it to the constriction of the chest, and the rupture of the channel of the perineum, and at all times, and with repletion; and you must press upon it, because if it holds too tightly, it causes obstruction or stomach upset and in the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations on the two sides of the neck are worth for the pains in the head, and the eyeache and the migraine, and with strangulation, and the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the sinew of the basilic vein; and you must command the surgeon that he stretch out his hand to put it, so that he does not touch the artery and do not make a sudden flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The bleedings under the chin are worth for mouth diseases and corruption of gums and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of blood-lettings from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bleedings under the armpits are worth for diseases that come from heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and command the surgeon that he not pierce too far in depth, because the place is bare of flesh, and lies over nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is above the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath, and it is necessary that the leech be big and made of iron, so that it can suck well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs bleed openly, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and they clean out the flowers; and they replace the two saphene veins and the two ankle veins, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and make a person more susceptible to fainting in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the leech is to put it on first empty, and let it suck in a timely manner, and then place it hastily, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redder of the blood; then pierce, and replace the leeches, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are such people who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice with only one prick.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to let out a great deal of blood, then we should do so often; and if the blood is thick, then make incisions deep and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it becomes necessary for those with tough skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the areas of cupping glasses with a stimulating and dissolving oil: if it's in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or melon seed oil; and if it's in winter, with valerian oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the residue is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom we apply treatment has soft skin and large pores, then it is not necessary to put oil on them, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or morellet water, or melon seed water, or porcelain nut water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very damp, should rise with ease, or rose water, and myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have great swellings should rise from old wine, or vinegar of wormwood, or a decoction of hawthorn or chamomile, or similar things; and do not think themselves healed by cupping before bathing or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep afterwards, and it is necessary that they warm up when they should be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are choleric and have too hot and inflamed blood; it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things; and drink vinegar, and flesh of goat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and middle-aged wine, which is between old and new, and drink vinegar of pomegranate, and vinegar of wormwood and small birds and young pigeons; and the day that they will be cupped, it is necessary to drink more than eat; and for some men it is necessary to give treacle or muscade before the cupping, or after, in order to comfort the main members; but it must be subtle with the blood, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The venesections that are done without causing pain are those that are placed over the liver, and over the spleen, and gout, and over the belly and the navel and the reins and the thigh, because those members do not suffer being cut thereon, and it is only done for drawing blood from member to member, as we place them over the breasts when they bleed; to remove the viscosity that is on the member, as we place venesections over the belly and over the navel to reduce the swelling; and take away the pain, when there is inflammation or stone, it takes away by its attractive virtue possibly the inflammation, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when one places it over the liver and over the spleen when there is retained moisture, and these venesections are administered empty to suck for a long time alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water, as in diseases of the eye, and in such manner that one fills the venesection with hot water solely, or with water where there are cooked herbs that are good for them.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the leech administered with fire is such:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The cautery instrument must be of wide and a half-palm depth, with the handle on one side around the middle in a small hole, just as to hold a needle, and it should be made of brass, soft in front so that it does not cut the patient when placing on the limb; and there should be inside the handle a crosswise iron or brass rod to place a candle under compression, and they must have great and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for children's ventouses are other than old people's, and thin people's than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.
