And one must put this ventouse thus on the limb: light the candle with wax or ointment and place it inside the ventouse at the crossing of the rod which is in the ventouse, so that the brightness is at the bottom of the ventouse so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and it should be above the pustule that we have said, so that when you want to remove the vapor, take off the ventouse; and apply the ointment as before, and do it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse which is administered for the disease of pleurisy, at all times sharp, does not have a verge nor a perforation, and is not used except when it is full of sharpness, and is placed on the member as such; and that's its shape.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Bloodsuckers are not used except in members where one cannot put bloodletting cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in uncovered areas without flesh, such as toes or nails, and others similar to them; and the quality of the user is that when you find bloodsuckers that are in sweet clear liquid due to a pustule, take them; and put one into a sweet clear liquid so they become famished, and have nothing in their bellies; and then be cleansed with vinegar and bloodletting cup, then rub the member until it becomes red, and put on the bloodsuckers; and when they are full and swollen, if that is a place where one can put a bloodletting cup, put them there, for this is worth a lot afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not so, then loosen the place with oil and then with vinegar, very well, and then apply a poultice; and if the wound festers too soon on the surface of the skin, moisten the linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the discharge is dried up; and if there are many discharges, put on vitriol or galls, or similar things, until they dry up; or put a mixture of peeled peas on the place, and leave them until they burn into the place, and will now stop bleeding; and if you need more, take other compresses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the discharges do not take hold, then rub the place of fresh blood on it, or you put a needle in so that the discharge comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick; and when you see that they are bleeding, powder some aloes and burnt silk, or ashes, over them, and they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a restoration of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear son, that the foolish wise men run away from this chapter, for they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read a letter about it; and because of this reason is the science estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, or which I have studied so much that I treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have written to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought forth, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book the contents and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding and remains on virtue, so that those who have been proven know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that whenever a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the patient on one side and on another, unless something else hinders you, such as weakness of body, childhood, or old age; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and apply cold compresses, that is to say, cool poultices, and meat from hare and goat, and let him not drink wine, nor eat any fat meats, and fill himself not too full of foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a warm abscess, or spreading of matter in the member; then recover the patient to his former governance which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to recover, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with meats that make thick nourishment or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and cheese, and bread, and bacon, and eggs, and fresh fat fish, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the bones repair themselves more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set or joined according to their nature due to the heat of the members, nor also those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, straighten over the broken bone large splints which have been seasoned and join the member together, until it strengthens itself like before; and do not remove all of your effort, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the back or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur to the radius, and others in twisting, such as the break of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with a small split or crack all the way through.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And it should have its device and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes back into place; and it is known that there is a break in the bone by what is twisted out of place, and it appears well on the outside, and sounds with pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but it may well have twisting, or fracture, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move the joint with the hand, but apply medicines that will come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that goes in a circle, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them at an equal point, just as abscesses grow closed; and if abscesses arise, let it be left alone for a day, until the abscess is soothed; then set it back to its place where you can easily and securely, and know that the restoration of it is more easy than the restorations of that which has pieces; then hold it, as it is necessary later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it holds together by two parts, whether it is hands or feet, or on your hand it is a small member, or on two strings, or with one string and on your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are freed, you reset by all means the additions in their places at the joint where you can, and beware that through your work does not cause the patient injury or pain; and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if you think it's not well, feel with your hand and straighten it gently, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring by their work hot apostemes and contractions to the member, which we have warned of many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, so chastise the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and beware well that the member be so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put him in such a condition that he feels no pain; and take care that he be put straightly, so that there is no twisting when he is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and thighs and similar: so it is necessary to envelop them in cloths of soft and fine linen; and those that are large, such as calves and legs: so it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole large member and hold it steady from all sides, without any slackness; then tie light dressings around three or four turns according to the member, and hold with your hand a stick at the entire bandage, then go up above the break and hold it less tight, so that the break will move away a little; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a great part of the healthy place, then take the other bandage, and turn around again over the broken place; then go back to the lower part of the break, and hold it moderately, not too tight nor too loosely, as we have said in the first lesson above; then put between the bands linings or cloths until they are completely even, then tie everything with a strip on top, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if he has an swelling or abscess, then put a soothing paste over the abscess hot and which draws out the swelling, and let it stay thus for some days; then tie on to the parts stars made of half a thick rope cord, or of wood from which one makes skewers, or of palm fibres, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the strap which you put over the breakage be a bit thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it needs to fit the member of small or great size; then tie on the straps in the same way as you did at the first bandaging, then tie above with a thread moderately tight, like in the first bandaging over the break; the tighter, the less so; and it is necessary that the thread be middle-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have more than one or two fingers breadth between each strap.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is scratched by the threads of the pads after they have been tied on in their healthy places, he should put under them strips of linen or chopped fleece so that he does not get hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is together with the fracture and the nerves are broken, I will say the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind all the broken members with pads on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, there is no need to apply poultices until after five or seven days, or more according to your safety from hot swelling; and behold here the manner of ancient ointments for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg white, and apply this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the ointment restoring breakage to many dispositions, and likewise for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of ointment restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take 30 aloe, and ladani, and enule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and myrrh, each 10; myrrh and aloes, each 5; alechil, 8. And make them into powder, and mix with plenty of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this ointment, for it has a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is worth for twisting: take myrrh and wormwood, one pound each; mirre and aloes, nine pounds each; mastich eight pounds; Armenian balm ten pounds, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plasters for joints and the bones dislocated from their places, and to soothe the pain occurring, and the breaking of the bone: take new linen, and soak it in oil and cooked grease, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment that heals broken bones: take dry leaves of fig tree and leaves of terrestrial plantain, and crush them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering to restore the breaking of the bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of balm, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches, each a part; and crush, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix with moisted water of coriander or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of bittersweet, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and sowbread, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says that the ointment to be put on a broken member in order to restore it strongly is nothing other than cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on a broken member in order to restore it, things that are slightly warm and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of ointment that is good for lesions and pain: take myrrh and chopped men's hair or bird quills, and valerian root, and equal parts, and crush them, and make an ointment with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the bandage a little afterwards, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it is not loosened for three days. And if there is pain at the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and unbandage, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sponge of the sea, and plunge in water, and lift up the joint, until the itching ceases, and the pain be calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it on a nut, as long as you are sure of hot swelling; and subdue the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then start the subtle bandage again, and a little poultice, and do not strain it so hard as before; and be subtle until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and effusion have been completely eliminated, and you need ointment and bandages again, then restart it, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes from the member of what we have said, then do not tie it except after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it twenty days, as is seen, until the swelling subsides, and approaches the flesh above; then restrain it more than before, and its meat becomes engorged, just as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that there will be no suppurating; loosen the tie with hot water every time you untie it, and let one drop of the liquid; by this work the swelling is cut off from the member, and quickly correct what the foolish physician does, who leaves the member twisted: it is bad, and it is a fearful treatment, and I see nothing else but to loosen and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems that we have reached the end of the text, which appears to be a medieval medical treatise on various types of bone fractures and their treatment.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures and various forms, and the causes are assigned; for there are fractures made by percussion with a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone down to the syphac that is under the bone, as done by a hatchet or axe; and because of this it is called this way of fracture "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and this kind of break is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two breaks is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact driven in, or a split, or a blow with a stone fist, or falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a pressing break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has healed in the bone as subtly as a scab, and the crack is small, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by being struck with a stone or by falling, or something similar, and causes the piece of the bone to enter downward, and the place becomes hollow like when cauldrons are heated over hot fires; the stone enters in.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft bones in the head, such as an infant's; and it occurs in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are pulled out like that; and I will speak of this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the kinds of breaks by the description above them, and the investigation that has been done, and through the spoiled flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently with a finger, if the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful about the bad accidents that can happen to the patient. And if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, paralysis, feverishness, and the eyes coming out red and inflamed, and other similar symptoms in more severe conditions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightful accidents and you hope for recovery, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first and it's in winter, it is advisable to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane under the bone doesn't become corrupted, and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus; and take hold of the patient's head injured, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if hemorrhaging comes out to reveal the bone, or a boil forms, have the aid of those it is necessary for, and be sure to stop the bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut with a sharp knife close before, and this shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions of different widths, some narrow and others wide, with points of iron indented, and work lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer incisions with awls, not too deep that they do not penetrate through the head of the bone; and there should be above the point a margin or a circle, that does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each one goes in its place on the edge of the bone, so that you have awls for all the head; and this is the shape of the three ways of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one awl on the bone and turn it back and forth until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then put the awl in a different place a little later, and do this all around, then cut with the forceps the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do it as subtly and lightly as possible, just as we have said, so that you can extract the bone with your hand or with any of the instruments that you have such as tweezers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, then it is necessary that you take out the splinter which remains from the bone with any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be sharper and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, lightly scrape them off with instruments; then cure the wound with stitches and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of surgery that Galen says is more sure; and he speaks very highly of it, and it is his own word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break is most apparent, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incision [the instrument], in whose form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut from one side, and the part of the body is inflamed in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you lightly score all around the bone, and take good care to avoid the membrane underneath; if it adheres to the bone, then scrape it lightly, for one scrapes well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not penetrate as far as the membrane, and the bone is chopped so only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to cover that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle rasp which you should have in various quantities, so that you can use them in each place where it seems most convenient, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rub with coarse rasps, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and fine breaks, it is necessary that you smooth out according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be attributed to someone who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the swelling is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound and moisten it in rose oil and place it over the wound; then take another linen doubled in two or three layers and moisten it in wine and rose oil and place it on top of the first linen; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not injure the swelling, then apply by means of the other bandage and do not bind it too tightly until it only closes the wound; and leave it thus for one day or two, until the abscess has been alleviated, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flax flour, frankincense powder, aristology, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and place it on the wound, and administer gentle medicines without cauterization; and be careful that the wound is completely clean, so that you do not leave ointment or allow stitches to remain, for when the stitches come together over the brain cloth, they will cause it to rot and become inflamed, and the patient will suffer great harm; for when one places something biting on the swelling, it hardens above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no good comes from the medicine that we have put on it, which is of such virtue, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and mix one drop with it; then apply the poultice to the wound.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that when the two parts of the nose above are broken or one by itself, for they are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous and does not break, so it does not cause more harm to bind or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must push your little finger or a perforated needle into it and insert that break even with your middle finger at the back of the joint; and let the nail grow back according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient feels no pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and cannot be reached by the probe, it is necessary for you to put a small cork or plug there at the head of a reed, about a finger thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do it again, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; if not, afterwards on the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then press a linen rag onto the head of the nail, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side if it is there; and let the cloths be so thick that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said a certain physician that one must moisten the tents with lard, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem to me that it's well, but it is necessary that they are moistened in the making of a poultice of almond milk and egg, and of flour; then leave the tent, until the bone is hardened, and the cartilage is strengthened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at times one places an oven or goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is .i. [one] sheet around it, and the patient holds the breath, and blows the patient through; therefore make the hole that you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to a boil while you are doing it, then put linseed oil or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in one pod of dragon's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling does not come, then put an ointment outside, of barley flour and incense powder, mixed with almond milk and egg; then place on light embers, and do not bind it tightly; and if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it to suitable tools for this, then cut the crack, and cure of things that are torn apart flesh, and soldering, such as ointments and unguents suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the bone, then heal it with poultices, and put linseed cakes on it, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is broken beneath and there is no wound outside, and the break is outside only so slightly, and it is not broken in two, rather bent inward, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you press your middle finger into the mouth of the sick person; and if the break is on the left jaw, then press your middle finger of the right hand, and press the break inward lightly, and shape it with the other hand from outside, and set it equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the lower jaw is spread in two parts, it is necessary that you provide an extension of two parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth has happened or breaking, then pull them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw wax, and on one double cloth; and put on the cloth a strong strap well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth that you can, and command the sick person to rest, and give them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the face changes, then release it on the third day, and then reattach what has changed; and put a plaster on, of flour dust with plenty of egg or linseed meal, after you have removed the wax; and put on a light linen cloth, and if the plaster dries and the condition of the sick person does not change, leave it alone until it is healed. Many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling appears, administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it is a break and wound together, reward no part of the bone is removed; unless carefully with suitable instruments to extract.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so that it enlarges with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is no more to remove, then close the wound, if it is wide, and put on one or two ointments suitable for this, to bring out pus, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The clavicle breaks in several places before the shoulder, and the break is in three manners: either it is broken and disjointed into two, with parts, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the aid that feels the broken clavicle; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the break between your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded staff made of cloth or linen, and as thick as needed; and stretch and hold the clavicle, and restrain the staff with your hand, so that you can put the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the clavicle outwards because it comes forward, then it is fitting that the patient lies on their side near their bed, and places a bolster under the shoulder; and have the assistants push the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the clavicle is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find that it is disjointed, it is fitting that you split it apart; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join together with any manipulation, then cut at one of the incisors that you have; but place under the clavicle this instrument, in order to protect the skin.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	it seems a spoon, and is not a cheekbone, and be as wide as it is necessary to cover the bone and the work; and have two knobs, so you see, and one is broad, and the other is narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you broke the bones; and when you are sure there is a hot abscess, cover the wound, and if the incision is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, sew up the wound with cloth and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses with a foul odor come, soak a cloth in oil of roses and lily and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	the binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you put powder from the mill and almond oil on the bone, and put light bandages on top, and a spear under the saddle, if necessary; then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put double cloth on top of the bandages, and the poultice; then take a thin rod three inches long and an inch wide, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage are hanging; and place the rod on the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the sound joint, and under the diseased joint; and remove it from each part, and when you see that the binding holds the break well, and you see clearly that the rod does not move over the broken bone, then reward it with a new one each day, and when the bindings loosen, hold them tight; and have the patient sit on his back, and place a small pillow under the saddle to raise the joint high; this will lighten the break of the collarbone by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents come, until twenty days; then reapply the poultice if you see that it is necessary, and bind it tight and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	C'est fini ! Merci pour la traduction de ce texte médiéval sur la réduction d'une fracture d'épaule. Si vous voulez en savoir plus, je peux essayer de traduire un autre texte ou de fournir des informations générales sur le sujet.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder blade breaks or widens its place, and we do not know what to do except by touching it; if it heals according to the figure of the breakage, and resets itself in its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put powder from the mill with abundance of egg and lightweight poultices on the place; then put a wide and subtle strip above it, one pace wider than the shoulder, and under the strip there are stitches in any part of the shoulder, so that you tie together the hairs of the strips of linen, so that the strip stays evenly; and then bind all tightly with a strong bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and look at it every day; and each time it heals, then bind it again, and put the strip even if it has gotten out of place, and rest the patient on their side; and the shoulder blade is restored in 20 days or in 25. And when this number is completed, then loosen it, and be sure, for it is not bone that gets loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes in front and points below the skin, then lift up, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the boil to calm the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the swelling (or possibly "the pus")
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, then it leans downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks flesh, and swells, and by chance may spit blood, and the veins appear in the broken bone, and they seem quite bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and puts .i. cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two collarbones with his hands, and gently places it in every way you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then puts plaster and bandages on top of the thin layer of salt or other light wood, and wraps it up in .i. cloth, and ties it around the broken bone so that it doesn't move; and turns the cord around to the back, and tightens it gradually, and rewards every hour with oil, and if it swells, then tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and clean the plaster, and address what has come there in manners of cures; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Note that the breaking of the ribs does not occur unless they are very large after the back, and at the head within, and only bend forward because they are greasy; and it looks good at the examination on the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set it even with the break, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a poultice and bind with an iron band if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inclining inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncturing, as well as tears, because the bone pierces the skin; and swells with blisters, vomits a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have applied a great device.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the stomach, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot pustules come, if it has not arrived yet.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they among us said that one applies cupping glasses on the place, in order to draw out thoroughly, and it seems like reason; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass may attract impurities to the place due to weakness of constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they among us said that the place should be covered with damp linen soaked in hot oil, and tents are put between the ribs to make equal heat all around, then it should be treated with the treatment of pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear because of the bone which sticks through the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then you must cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath a tool to hold back the spleen; and then you must saw the bone, and pull out lightly, and then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess forms, put moistened cloths soaked in rose oil on it and apply them to the place; and cure the wound while holding steady the part that needs the abscess, and be careful over the surrounding area where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	It seems like we've finished this passage! The text appears to be a medieval medical treatise on how to treat various injuries and conditions, including fractures and dislocations.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally comes fracture to both bones of the collar, and it occurs when they bend; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then observe closely if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, it does not hurt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you restrain them and prick, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been cured, if you put a cure there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it has been healed or not, then observe closely if the feet are softened, and if the parts that are in the hands are swollen, and on the back there is ventosity and ejection without volition; and when one has relieved them on their stomach, if there is ejection without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is certain that it is mortal: the patient will not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is much lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is hot swelling, to put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is calmed; then put on one of the soothing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are broken, it is necessary to cover with a poultice; and take out the bone, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam; then cure with ointment dripping grease until he is healed. And if there is a crack in the bone, called the "bone's eye", put your left hand pouch into it and place it equal to the other hand's power, then apply the plaster and the splint if necessary; then bind it tight, and if there are broken bones, make them whole again, take out the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	This appears to be a title or heading in Middle French, which translates to:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, then there will be a slight diminishment to the head; and they become too long, and incline towards the middle, and come to the patient with pain at the place, and swelling, and inflammation of what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand up so high that it reaches the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is at the head alone, then put the same breakage in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is too long, or it inclines towards the inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of this breakage becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put on a splint, then put on a stick of wood or iron, and bind the breakage, so that it does not move; and place the splint under the ribs, until the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and then put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as needed, if there is no bad accident; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The breakage of the arm (or shoulder). This appears to be a medieval medical text discussing various types of injuries and their treatment, specifically fractures and dislocations. The text is written in Old French and includes detailed descriptions of symptoms, treatments, and post-operative care.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The arm (or shoulder) is what lies between the armpit and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways: one being that you take a straight stick of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders together with two strings, and hang them up high, and instruct the patient to sit on one seat; then throw a broken arm over the log so that it comes in line, and place a wooden support in the middle of it, then hang something heavy or have the servants hold it down below; then put the splint level with his hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you strap the patient on their bed, and tie their hand to their neck, then command two servants to have one stretch what is on the splint to his hands, and the other to stretch underneath all of each string, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, hold the strap under the splint, and above the splint, and stretch each of the attendants to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the splint is near to the head of the shoulder, you must put the middle strap under the arm, and the other towards the armpit, under the splint; and similarly if the splint is towards the armpit, it is necessary to put the lighter strap slightly, without effort, until the splint is level on the place, and on the armpit; then make it equal as needed, and hold it tight, lest a swelling come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a swelling comes, do not strain it for 7 days, and put a warm compress on the splint and in olive oil rose, until the swelling is calmed; then strain it, and the way to strain it is that you put the splint on the arm, then bring the arm up onto the elbow support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put a cloth over it, and strain on the elbow and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is out of place.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not in place, use strapping (steles), and put a thicker and stronger strap on the splint, and space them apart by two fingers, so that each strap is as long as it reaches three finger breadths from each side; then strain on the straps, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the splint, but more strongly and less loose.
