Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seating of the stars, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the warm abscess, so let it be tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days at the bandage, lest pruritus or inflammation comes to the place, or swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the arm, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes to it, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back and have their hands on their stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion made of equal wool, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken member does not move, or become loose the ligaments; if the arm recovers through the power of medicine, and give it the food we have mentioned before, in such a manner that the food is at the first subtleties; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in forty days from then; and then one must loosen and administer bath and ointment medicaments to bring the place back into order.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the swelling is ugly and stuck, it should stay untied for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones called the "foscile", one small and one large, with the smaller one near the shoulder and the larger one below, towards the elbow. Perhaps the larger bone breaks alone or the smaller one, or perhaps both at once.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the great ones are broken, it is bad healing, and more grievous than when they were broken together at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone alone that is broken, then it should be slightly stretched and made straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great bone, then it should be strained more strongly; and stretch him on a cushion, and bind his hand to the highest part of the other's arm, and the little ones lower than the others, and that the patient may not feel any pain; then extend one of the attendants' arms under his hand, or at the elbow, and another attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors equal, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has caused fragments to be separated, then put each one back in its place. And if there's no loose piece that can be grasped and restored to its place, then do as we said before: operate (or "let an oste" - let a surgeon) on it.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is also an open wound, I have spoken separately about the treatment of that in the chapter on singular cases; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment a cold abscess appears, then apply a cloth made from rose oil and white wax, that it not be too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth on top carefully, until the cold abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and I put on the poultice of mill powder with plenty of egg white; then put on the stars, and let the star of the breakage be at once stronger and a little bit larger than the others; and know that it should have six stars or arms in more dispositions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and hold the breakage higher than anywhere else, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths on top of the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the string with which it is held be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching which comes to the member, then you must fumigate the member with hot water, so that those itches are calmed down; and let the member not be tightly still.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the splinting, and if the ligament is loose and the bone disjointed, and similar thing, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take note that the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, take care to soften it a little bit, and then let it be for some days until the swelling comes back, and then strain again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not loosen him until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or then loosen the bandage around him, and let his hands hang at his neck, and be his collars even, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this breakage is restored in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	It seems we've reached the end of a medical text about bone fractures.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on both thumbs there are small breaks, and it often rains with many drops.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the tip of the hand is broken or swollen, it is necessary that the patient crosses his legs and sits straight in front of him; then he puts his hand on the stretched cloth and stretches the broken bones so they are even with each other as much as possible; and applies an ointment and bandages, if there are swelling, then he wraps a linen sheet according to the quantity of the injury.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the navel of the hand, he makes a sphere with linen and orders the patient to press it against his broken hand; and then binds it with a long sheet, and so that the bandage is as wide as the hand, and it is bound, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the end, it is necessary that you put a bandage on top and another underneath in the hand, so that the fingers are open and straight; then bind the entire hand tightly, and tie the string between the thumbs.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the thumbs, if it's a simple break, tie them even and as necessary; bind the hand with the broken thumb together, and if you see that you put a small straight bandage to lift the break, and don't move it. And if the break is on other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, tie them even and bind them with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all in one hold, which is useful, or place a bandage over it as you would for a boil; and take note of the restoration and arrangement of applying warm compresses, and secure what comes to it, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons terminé la traduction de ce texte médical ancien. Si vous souhaitez poursuivre avec un autre extrait, n'hésitez pas à le partager !
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	Et c'est là que l'on remarque souvent les fractures de la cuisse, car elles sont fréquentes ; et la guérison s'effectue en attachant une ficelle au-dessus de la fracture, et une autre dessous.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	Et le malade repose sur son lit, puis étend chacun des membres avec une égale tension ; et c'est à ce moment-là que la fracture se produit dans les os.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the scrotum, so that one of the ligaments goes towards the testicle, and the other ligaments are under the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and then so be the ligament next to the kneecap, and so be the extension below; then place the miter on the bone in both hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and the bandage, lest an abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	Et s'il y a un abcès chaud, laissez-le se cicatriser, puis revenez à votre travail et à votre traitement ; la liaison ou l'attelle est faite de même manière.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It behooves you to wrap the break with a strong double bandage in two or three layers, and remove any surplus, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and tie a long thread between the scrotum and the leg, next to the kneecap below, and have the end of the thread come up; then turn back on the leg and on the scrotum the bandage, then place stars on the break, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then tie the easy drape between the leg and the scrotum for an even constriction, then begin to tie tightly three turns or four above the break; and as you go up from the break, so loosen the constriction; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you tied between the leg and the scrotum, and tie three stars above, then return to the bottom at the end of the thread, until you come next to the foot; and it constricts, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, lest there come an abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Et si il y a infection, alors déliez l'étau, adressez-vous à ce qui se produit, comme nous l'avons dit maintes fois ; et s'il y a des fragments d'os qui se projettent, il convient de les ramasser, autant qu'on peut.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at any time the skin is broken thus where stars are put in as in an injury and the arm; however, in this restoration made it does not ring out for the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the skin is restored in one day or a little less or a little more according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the shoulder joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is much breakage, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is only a fissure or a hole, and there is no wound, nor without a wound, and that seems very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus when you put back in place all that was torn at its joints, as long as it can be assembled; then apply the plaster, and I would put a rounded star on it if needed, and then tighten everything as it should be; then reward all the preparations we have said for other breaks, such as applying heat and similar remedies; and for each accident you put what is necessary until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by the right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all another breakage as when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is so, and the work is entirely the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns of all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it can be seen well; and it turns beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer an extension, and place it straight, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many fragments, that the extension be less and more light; and lift according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wooden rods that stretch from one end of the leg to the other, from the knee down to below; then wrap them in two loops with a bandage, one above and one below, and tie it all together in the middle. And at this point, the leg cannot lean to the right or to the left, and thus it is well. Some also provide a splint of the same length as the leg, made of wood, and put the leg in it to hold it steady and properly treat the break or wound. And move each day the leg, to see if there is hot swelling or other accident; and care for it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not often break, but the bones of the foot sometimes do, and you must pay attention, for there is no cure in most cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break, and you see the bones overlapping one another, then put the sick foot on the ground, as if it were going to jump, and then place your other foot on top of it, where the bones are raised, and then press down so that they return to their proper place. Then apply an ointment and bandages, and under the foot of the injured person, a small block with two flat surfaces, and tie it securely to the foot in such a way that the injured part is supported; once you have wrapped everything properly, and done all that you need to do.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, then untie the bandages, for you will find that the bones are back in place, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any toes that are broken, restore them as we have said about the fingers of the hand. Then take a splint for the broken toe and tie it with a string according to its length, making it a little thicker, and then put under the foot the block I mentioned earlier, and secure it firmly in place. And if there are two or three, or more, toes that are broken, then take a separate string for each toe and wrap them together in a piece of linen cloth, and tie the block to the foot securely, so that it is well in place at the head of the block, away from the foot's skin.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things I've said about other breaks, which we've discussed; and provide care for each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the wrist (or forearm)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, so it makes her sit upright and enlarge it, then incline to the part at the back, and have it held from behind; then fill the natural pouch of the patient with cotton, and put as much in it as I can [hold]; then take the woman up and lift up the lower back a little bit by little bit, and thus jump the cotton, so that it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with the same shape; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: then the break will be restored, and if you wish, take a bladder of plants, and tie a cord to the navel, and pour all the bladder into nature; then blow in the cord firmly, so that the bladder is blown out inside: nature will return the bone; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it be healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the shoulder blade of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the hip bone; and these recent breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and use into it and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For fractures signify many different conditions in the right way of restoration: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's girth and put the penis into it; then bind it with cloth around, and let it be so for three days or longer, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with an open wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a fracture with an open wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the thigh or the armpit or similar, that he be sutured now, so that the sutures which we have mentioned may bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the bone remains brittle from vitriol, then if you have no other choice, start to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, before a swelling comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a swelling comes, then leave the restoration just until the fifth day, so that the swelling is calmed down, and don't touch it for another third or quarter of a day, because you would bring on a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed above the skin and visible, it's necessary that you cover it with a light dressing in your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	Et se li extensions ne t'est apparillie pour mettre egal a tes mains, si leve le ramoingne avec cet instrument qui est de fer, qui a 7 doigts ou 8 de long, et la largeur est selon la quantité de la plaie. Et pour cela est nécessaire au maire qu'il emprunte 3 ou 4, selon ce qu'il en a besoin en chacune cure de fracture; et soit rond et un peu gros, qui ne plie mie à la compression sur le membre à ton ouvrage, et soit aiguisé devant, et grossi du milieu en avant, ainsi:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palinche", for which reason the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and tie it once, as long as it will hold, and make them equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the end of the bone, as long as the instrument has control.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, then use a suitable instrument, such as a chisel or saw, at your disposal; then remove what remains in the bone from sharpness and small scabs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with black vinegar and properly tie it; and do not put cerote or any other ointment on the wound so that you cause infection and corruption; then administer remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing all around according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not held back with the breakage; and many foolish physicians have done this, and brought death or corruption upon the patient sometimes; and the dressings are more gentle and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents will come of it, as we have said, and you find pain in its place, then it does not seem good to put on dressings; but envelop around, instead of dressings, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the pus growing in the wound, then take out what you have put on it of all wine, and put on salving ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the bandage on the member two times a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is bound and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the bowing goes downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it has been many days and cannot heal but rather keeps bowing, know that there are small bones inside, which is why you should seek the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose bone fragments that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what he says in his chapter here before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and shows on the member, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and similar ones in the great members, then do not take it out, for many times death occurs, but let it alone until it becomes rotten; perchance it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The swellings that come on the sore. (This appears to be a quote from a medieval medical text, possibly related to the treatment of wounds or injuries.)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We see many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the swelling is fresh: administer purgative medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, either separately or together, and mix them with a purging wine or with egg whites or with vinegar; and apply them to the sore in poultices, and strain it well, and do not loosen it for a day; then loosen it and repeat another one, until the swelling is gone; or you may apply it on a well-made piece of cloth; for the property of cloth is that it removes all the swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut off the excess, or have it cut by a surgeon, until it is gone, and cure the wound as long as it remains healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which is weak after recovery. (This phrase suggests that the text may be discussing the treatment or care of a patient who has experienced physical weakness or debilitation after recovering from an illness or injury.)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is healed and there remains after the member weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not as tight as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to a multitude of swelling; or due to excessive movement, neither in its right time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great nourishment, and washes it often with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the member twisted after healing. (This phrase suggests that the text may be discussing the treatment or care of a patient who has experienced physical deformity or twisting of a limb after recovering from an injury or illness.)
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, although its natural function is not lost: do not believe the foolish people who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great evils, and perhaps death. However, if the nodules and tortures are fresh, it is necessary to remove them with warm water, or herbs that soften, such as mullein leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the musilage of mullein, mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top. Or take fatty figs, grind them with coltsfoot seeds, and similar medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is taken out because of constant and long rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened and turned into stone-like hardness, and it needs to be removed with a knife, then cut just up to the bone, carefully and lightly with a sharp razor. And cover with a compress and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here starts the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it must be returned to its proper place immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling grows and by chance puts pressure on the joint; therefore it is not fitting to move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times brings forth abscesses and other pains; nevertheless, when this occurs, if the patient's condition improves, then let him rest until the abscess has been alleviated; then heat the member with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have outlined the chapters on dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	What happens when the jaws are dislocated and they hang down, and the dislocation of both is in two manners: either they are slightly out of their place and softened a bit; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva from the mouth drips and it cannot hold its mouth closed, nor can it enclose its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to place on its own within a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and completed, you should reset it quickly, and not delay; and in this way that the attendants show the patient's head, and thrust the mirror's spoon from one of their hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are outside to put it straight; and instruct the patient to loosen, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts the mirror or spoon pouch into place until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw does not return easily, even if it is both jaws together, then one raises them with hot water and oil, until they are cleaned lightly; nor delay in returning the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment, and the patient's mouth is closed well with a softening agent, then place damp cloths on it made from rose oil and wax; and tie them loosely with moist threads; and the patient lies on their back, with their head between two pillows, so that it does not move to either side nor make any effort to chew; but take light food until the pains are removed, and have the jaws be closed; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not work at opening the mouth to eat or drink, as long as the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then it comes to fever and severe pains, and possibly a diarrhea, and perhaps a vomiting of cold pure liquid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a bad sign; and many times death comes to the person in whom this occurs within 8 days.
de la forcelle	the dislocation of the jaw (from the previous text)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot descend from the cheekbone to the jawbone and is easily felt when it occurs.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and stretches out their arms; and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will come back; then apply the plaster and bandage, and hold it; and the shoulder blade which is near the spine cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does dislocate at any time, you must reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and hold it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and in the same way the shoulder blade is brought back when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way is when it slips out of its socket below; and the second way is when it comes out from under the bone; and perhaps it slips out from on top, and this happens often; and it does not come loose behind for the shoulder, and it does not become loose inside for the nerves; and it slips out towards the socket many times, especially in those who have a lot of flesh, for then it leaps out suddenly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out slowly, and goes back slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens that some men have a blow or bruise, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you should examine it carefully until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the shoulder dislocation occurs when it falls towards the socket, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them manifest diversity; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the socket on the side of the top of the shoulder, just as if there were an owl's nest; and the patient cannot return their hand to its place, nor move with any movement; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not easily cured when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician lifts the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the armrest, and forces the joint back to its place with great force; and the physician lifts the hand and stretches it upwards, then places it down again, and it will come into place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in the hands within a few days, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and the assistant will rise soothing and calming, as decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilotus in water, and will bring it; then the patient is to be laid on his back, and put under the arm a linen pad equal, not too soft nor too hard, then place the mirror at the patient's heel on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder properly, and pull the patient's hand; and another assistant will grasp the patient's head so that it does not move downward; immediately the shoulder comes back, and if you see that you must reset it in this manner: and that you make a man present who is larger than the patient; and stand on the side of the patient, and push his shoulder under the arm of the patient, and lift the arm up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant will pull the patient's hand downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then he may carry something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is also done in another way: and it's like this: you stick a long stick in the ground, so that its top is as thick as a fist, and not too big or too small; then it is placed under the patient, but wrapped so softly on top, and the patient is leaning against the length of the wood; then his hand is stretched out from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return because of all the things we have said, do this cure: take a stick with two arms and four inches wide, which has its top pointed so that it can go into deep under the shoulder, in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then take the rope from above the beam and wrap it around the arm so that the arm is not injured; then place the patient's elbow under the arm; stretch his arm over the long beam, and tie the shoulder to the beam, and his hand at the tip of the hand, then put the arm on one shelf of a wooden splint wide enough, and have him stretch out his hands down, and let his body hang from the other side: the joint will be restored now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that you place under the arm a wooden staff of wool equal to it, then put the poultice around the powder from the mill with incense and onion broth over the entire shoulder and around, then apply the straining cloth under the arm carefully, and turn the string on the poultice, and encircle the hand around his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he drink broth until the limbs are comforted, because he will heal more quickly; and then drink more after five days or seven, and move him; and if it is firm and has not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in or for another reason, it is necessary for you to administer cauterizations at three pores, as they are shown before this chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it does not heal after seven days, and the joint does not hold together and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the chest or shoulders, or back, is caused by a blow and stretching of the hands, and it should be treated in another manner; and it cures as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes pain and stiffness in the member, and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until the pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	De la dislocation du coude ! (Il y a une marque d'exclamation qui manquait dans le texte original)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and especially before and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, for one sees it clearly and feels it clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the cut of the patient with the wound, so it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you treat it before the swelling comes, for if the swelling comes, it would be hard to reduce it; and perhaps it cannot be reduced completely at all, especially when it is behind; and it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the treatment is this, when it can be reduced to such a state that you can reduce it, that you stretch out his hand to your two hands; and his arm be spread wide, and the hands of the examiner according to the shoulder around, above and below, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, as long as it revives to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and puts pressure on the root of the palm on the joint that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and is that two ministers extend the arm, and bind it with two ministers, so it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when the physician has joined the jointure to her hand, she anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then binds the joint firmly, until it heals; and when it is back in place, she puts on dry plaster with the yolk of egg, and binds it firmly, and holds the arm at the neck of the patient, and leaves it for a few days, then unties.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, he releases the bandage and leaves it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, he re-applies the plaster and the bandage, and leaves it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then he releases it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and scrub him well, and press so that it is relieved; or put a lamb's fat cloth on the joint, then let it be for one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the cloth on it, and then have him enter the bath; and thus do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see that he needs it, put a warm moist linen poultice on him, and strain it over him; so it will return to its place.
