de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder joints
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	At times the joint of the hand is dislocated to each side, at times on the back of the palm or belly; then you must bind the joint and hold the dislocation in place until it recovers, then support the head of the joint, and move it towards the part where it was disjoined; and let it be for two days, and then make it equal on that day; and from then tie it, as we have said, and release it by day, and make it move, and re-tie it at night; and do this often, until it becomes tight, and do the same if it is dislocated to the belly of the hand, and do so as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the vertebrae of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are several that are dislocated, then there is no remedy, for the bone hastens to kill the sick person.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations jump out without will, nor can they be held, and many times soften some member, either the two hips or both arms or one; and often the shin moves to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "giltubositez": the cure is that you return if the giltubositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing whatsoever.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the old ways of cures by great words say it is not at all in great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the giltubositez that comes to the front of the chest, there is no cure nor health; and also that which comes straight down both sides, and one cannot cure those that come properly to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lies out on his face in an even place, and has a bandage under him so he does not bleed; then put two skewers into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a string between the patient's heels, and another at the hips, and thighs, and knees, and ankles; and two attendants should know how to tie the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two skewers; and they should be well closed, the skewers as we have said, and the physician put his palms on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a plank of three arm-lengths long, and shave the underside with it, and the patient be on their side, and put the head of the plank under the spot, then place the middle of the plank above the spine; and put the mirror so that its feet are on the other end of the plank, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it in a turn which turns back towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you make two skewers at the head of the patient of one arm-length long, and towards their feet two others, and between each skewer there should be a palm's breadth apart upwards and downwards; and in each skewer there is one hole, where the turnstick fits, and the skewers are firmly stuck in the ground so that they do not move; and between the two skewers there is one skewer turning, around which the turnstick turns, and it has two small skewers of a palm's breadth long to turn the turnstick; and then tie the cord that is among the armpits under the turnstick towards the head, and the other cord towards their feet to the other turnstick, and each of the attendants turns their turnstick to all the cord, and the master makes the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, so apply desiccating ointment with abundance of egg, and then bind it up, and then the stick from a tablet of three inches in length, which presses out the place of the hip joint and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient for subtle nourishment, until they are healed; and if any thing comes at the end of healing, so administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stick that we have mentioned before; and sometimes administer one piece of cloth, and once the appearance comes in the rear part of the spine next to the back, and think one that it is dislocation; and it is the bone which opens up, for which one should not have presumption: perhaps would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Displacements of the shoulder joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that the joints of the shoulder and the joints of the arm do not come out without dislocations only, nor does it happen as with other joints; and the joint of the shoulder is displaced in four ways: inward and outward, and forward and backward; and more inward thus, and less outward forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is such that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee joint opens up more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the place which is near the swollen area of the hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes outwards is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose it comes forward are that his leg feels well in accordance with its completion; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, holds back his urine, swells the groin, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose it comes behind are that he cannot straighten his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the level of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you should return to see if the dislocation is old and has remained in its position, and there is no cure; and one must not have presumptions.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four manners of dislocation, hasten to turn back the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and bend it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must have a strong minister come, and have the leg stretched out very hard with two hands, or on one lien tied above the knee; and another minister stretches their hand up in such a way that they press their hands under his buttocks, then he tightens him with a single lien above the thigh; and stretch everything up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground all at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to three signs, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not so, then you must apply treatment to its likeness. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, then it is necessary that you lift the patient on his healthy side, then put the lien above the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the armpit, then stretch the lien upwards towards the armpit, and towards the hip; then take another minister's arms, and encircle the thick part of the sick person's thigh, and extend it far out: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot compress it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft cord on both heels and on both shins, and let the sick leg be stretched out two fingers more than the others; then hang him from the top of a pole, and above the earth two arms long; then command the attendant to grasp the chief of the joint, and have another attendant hanging with the patient, who grasps firmly the joint, for the joint returns now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at its end, have the patient lie down as we have said in the case of gilbozitee, and loosen the cord above the sick leg properly, and on the hip also; then put two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert the torch between the joints into the patient inside the form; and have moistened cloths placed around so that he does not harm himself, then stretch out each attendant towards him, and the physician should place an equal mark on his hand where the dislocation is.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's well.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the gilbosection, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be stretched out quickly, and as I said; and place the mirror so that it hurts the patient's skin over the knee joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the elbow.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it does not seem good to stretch the patient downwards or lift him up on the earth, but rather he should be as if the hip was dislocated on the outside, as we have said about lying on two hips; and he should be on his back, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be right when the patient stretches out his legs, and they will be equal; then bring together the thighs, and put in a splint, and an elastic band to restrain the hip so that it does not move; and he should rest for three days or four, then loosen it, and put on a splint; and if you see that they are equal, then tighten again, as before, and let him rest for three days; then loosen it, and let him walk slowly, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	It seems we've reached the end of this medical text's section on joint dislocations.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward, outward, and behind; and do not come out in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg to their knee, and if it does not stay at their knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you sit the patient up straight, and extend their leg if they can, and put your back against their face, and place their foot on yours; then take their kneecap in your palms, and draw between your teeth, then bend the two sides of the kneecap together; and another assistant extends their foot, until the kneecap returns to its place, and the sign is that it stays well at the knee lightly; and put a poultice on it, and make the leg stay against the knee, and bind them tightly together for three days or four, then loosen them; and the patient should not move about, until the member is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not in place, then administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like we've moved on to a new topic.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it goes back to the part where it was dislocated; the return is easy, and you must stretch it gently with your hands when it has only just been set.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it has been set in place completely, then you must have the patient sit up straight, and the attendants will support him by the leg, above the ankle; then draw the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and push well the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and drawing the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned in this way, then have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix a wooden beam firmly on the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around him so that he does not harm himself; then the attendants will support the thigh, and another attendant will stretch the foot up with their hands or a strap, up to the ankle of the foot; then each attendant will stretch equally, and the beam will be between the patient's thighs to hold him when it is being stretched; then place the other attendants each hand on the dislocation, and another attendant will support the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is fixed in place, then put the plaster and bandages on top, and strain them firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and take care of the ligaments that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then let it be for two days or three, and if the ligament becomes loose, retighten it; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and keep the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before this term ends, it's no surety that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the swelling, you should drain it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	It looks like this text may be coming to an end! "Des dois" means something like "to the hands" or "as for what remains", but in this context, it's likely just a concluding phrase indicating that the instructions are finished. Is there anything else you'd like me to help with?
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulder is no longer swollen, it should be well-stretched without effort, and that's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any new place of the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table entirely straight, and put your foot on what appears of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is evened out, and there is nothing apparent, then put under the sole of the foot a table at two feet, then strain them firmly, and let it be for three days, then release it; and make him rest, until he is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at first soothing poultices on hot apostemes and leave the patient to God's hand if you don't see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place so that the hot aposteme comes; and when the member is in its place, administer soothing poultices on hot apostemes and cure the wound as it suits, with dry ointments; and if with dislocation there is breakage and small bones separated, then extract them and do what we have said about simple maladies; and beware of entering a path of fear, according to what I've said, for that will harm you according to your Creator, and on account of the knowledge to arm and protect your body.
Amen	So be it.
